when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的 , 是要說未來會比這更重要 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了亞特林 , 1936年 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , 巴bbage的機器完全是機械性的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這些人都是從數學的角度來的 , 但推特告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把數學基礎放在電腦科學上 , 然後說: 「 不論你怎麼製作一台電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論是電腦的機械裝置 , 像是babbage的機械裝置 , 或像現在的電腦 , 或在未來的細胞 , 或再一次 , 一旦我們進入奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	電腦的本質是這樣的 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做教堂主教論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你看到了這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage建造的真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們現今用電腦做的每件事 , 只能慢慢地 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你知道它有多慢 , 它有1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用紫色卡片 , 它被送進來 , 最初的zx81會慢一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一堆拉姆攻擊 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想加入更多的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有一些計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館檔案庫 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由charlesbabbage所寫 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 計畫28 」 的計畫 , 也是我一開始的慈善機構名字 , 他是科學博物館的管理員 , 也是驅動這個專案計畫創造出差異引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有許多零件可用 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一個是巴比奇的檔案檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是那台機器模擬的電腦 , 最後一部分就是在科學博物館裡建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它建造時 , 你終於可以理解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為不用在你面前的小晶片 , 你必須檢視這一大堆的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體運作 , 我看到cpu運作 , 我聽見它的運作 。 我可能聞到 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們會做模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴比斯自己寫下 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它將會引導未來科學的發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造它 , 因為他總是和新計劃結合 , 但當它在1940年代被建造出來時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我會給你們一些小品味 , 用影片來展示cpu機制的其中一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 它會加入 。 這是行動中的加入機制 , 所以你想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代之前 , 我們將會有它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這張照片中 , 雅恩•亞伯特蘭德展示了他最近期的三項專案 , 關於人類和我們的棲息地 , 在他的系列《地》中 , 來自世界各地的個人訪問 , 《六十億個其他的網路專案》 , 以及他的小說: 「 家 」 , 透過呼吸的影片 , 記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、未來、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅恩•亞伯特蘭在寬角的地球上捕捉到脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對這個星球有很大的影響 , 可以通過飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談到生態學 , 我在一年內將二氧化碳排放成法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得要殺害法國人嗎 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來減碳 , 就像我每次都會做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看我去年拍攝的一些例子 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達沙石油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯塔人工作非營運24小時內 , 七個小時 , 盡可能地抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的末端 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用三倍的石油 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新加州的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	在2050年之前 , 百分之百的珊瑚會因為全球暖化而消失 。

the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	北極的厚度從1960年開始下降了超過40% 。

according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 一百年後 , 所有的山層冰河都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球的生命非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾說的 , 有20億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。

one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	人類的五分之一依賴魚來生存 。

intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集的農業正在耗盡土壤 。

the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這個例子裡 , 理查.雷斯尼克顯示了廉價和快速基因組定序將如何顛覆健康照護 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查.雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體是左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩個複製的x染色體 ; 男性有x , 當然 , y的複製小型複製 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉 , 男孩們 , 但這只是一個小小的小東西 , 讓你變得不一樣 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 那你會看到的是雙螺旋結構 , 生命的編碼由這四個生物化學字母拼出來 , 或者我們稱之為基礎:a、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少人 ? 三十億人 。
is that a big number ?	這是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	每個人都可以用大數字排出 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把一個像素放在1280-80-80-800的解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便說一下 , y染色體決定要定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	實際上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美金 , 基因組是序列 , 出版 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本被發表了 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一塊錢的成本很慢 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴你們 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 沒有人知道它 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以現在我們將基因組做50個複製 , 我們將這些複製片切成50個鹼基 , 然後我們將這些複製品進行大量的序列 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它帶到軟體中 , 重新組合它 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給你們一張圖片 , 人類基因組計劃:3gabes , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台在其中一台機器上跑:每週200gabases 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將要改變600年 , 沒有這種速度慢 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	基層的價格下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	等到2011年 , 等到2011年 , 你可以開到木星和兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc定位、醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、古老的定序方式 , 而這都是新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個邏輯規模 ; 你通常不會看到像那樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界的基因組排序的能力是今年大約五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們根據被放置的機器 , 來知道這一點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期兩倍、三倍或四倍的壽命 , 可預見的未來 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室代表了百分之二十的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學院 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國人絕對贏得這場新月球 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學的意義是什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她展示了第2種雌激素接受性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她回來了三階段三階段的卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再一次治療手術和化療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時得到更多卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她回來了有急性的愛滋病白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	八天後 , 她進入呼吸器失敗 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士被治療的過程 , 大約十年後 , 會看起來像血管般 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	是因為像我同事rickwilson這樣的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所 , 他決定去看這位女子的後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他將皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚和癌症骨髓序列序列列列列 , 並在幾個禮拜內完成了這兩個基因組 , 沒有什麼大不了的基因 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他將這兩組基因組比較在軟體中 , 他發現 , 其它的基因組 , 是一組退化 , 一組二千個鹼基 , 一個叫做tp53的基因組 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你的基因中有這種明顯的突變 , 你的生命中有90%可能罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這並不能幫助這位女士 , 但如果你願意的話 , 這對她的家庭有嚴重的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果牠們有同樣的突變 , 牠們會得到這種基因測驗 , 牠們會去定期的篩檢 , 牠們會早期發現癌症 , 可能活得更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我介紹一下bery雙胞胎 , 診斷出brebralsy的年齡 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是位非常勇敢的女性 , 不相信症狀不適合 , 透過一些英雄的努力和網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學社群 , 事實上 , 他們也有其他的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是多功能性的失調症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以 , 他們得到了 「 反光 」 , 而他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但它們並不完全符合症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片裡的先生是名叫joebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運能成為一家叫做生命科技的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家公司之一 , 製造這些巨大的基因組定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他拿到了他的孩子定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列的突變 , 叫做spr , 負責製造血清素的基因 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在東opa上 , 他們給了這些孩子一種血清素前的藥 , 他們現在很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有完整的基因序列 , 這永遠不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 它的成本是十萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美元 , 明年是一萬美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	一百元以後的那一年 , 給予一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是它移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和松槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	沒錯 , 尼克在兒童醫院出現這種異類的肚子 , 像是有名的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西時 , 他的腸道會打開 , 聞起來會流出腸道 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 。 我非常痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生發生在臨床遺傳學中 , 他不知道發生什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子的基因序列 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 一個單一的突變基因負責控制細胞死亡 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以理論是 , 他有一些免疫反應 , 基本上 , 食物的本質是 , 這是一種自然反應 , 導致某些細胞死亡 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫展示了他的骨髓 , 一個新的裝置 , 很快地收集了生命的骨髓 , 和捐贈者的最小疼痛 。 他強調 , 骨髓中的成人幹細胞可以被用來治療許多有用的疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟疾病 。

daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	丹尼爾克拉夫發明了更好的方式來收割骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是史丹佛大學的一名小兒科癌症醫師和幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床專注是骨髓移植 。

and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	骨髓其實是用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 大部分先進的惡魔 , 例如白血病、淋巴瘤和其他的疾病 。

we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 來拯救一個患有白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們到底該如何取得這個骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 普遍麻醉、護士 , 還有另一位醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	巴布在桌上 , 我們用這種小針 , 你知道 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法基本上是透過軟組織把它放進硬骨裡 , 進入管子裡 , 一個技術術語 , 每次都會用針筒刺穿十磅的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把它交給護士 。 她將它安靜下來 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 。 我們再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百倍 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	我的手臂末端 , 我手上有一通電話 , 更別說是bob , 他的耳端看起來像這樣 , 像是瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 這種手術在大約四十年來都沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	或許還有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個極端的侵入性方法 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦工 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	標記礦工是這樣運作的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準化患者 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨骼數十次 , 我們進入一次 , 進入髖部或臀部的前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、強大的導管 , 有一個特殊的迴圈 , 可以留在馬路的殘骸中 , 追蹤髖關節的路徑 , 當它四處移動時 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你非常快速地吸引人 , 或吸引 , 把骨髓很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過同樣的入口 , 做好幾次 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , 鮑勃只能拿到一根插座 , 當地的麻醉劑 , 將收成作為一個不夠久的劑量 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛有一點點理所當然 。
and played around with this a little bit .	玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有兩個大型動物和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們驚訝的發現 , 我們不僅得到骨髓 , 還得到了10倍的幹細胞活動 , 相較正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置是在去年核准的 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是活的病患 。 你可以看見它跟隨著靈活的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人身上 , 會有兩條路經過同樣的洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	在當地的麻醉劑中 , 做過這種事 , 作為一個外來的病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們又得到了三至六倍的幹細胞 , 比同一個病人所做的標準方法還要多三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的身體中 , 包括骨髓中的血液幹細胞 , 我們一直使用這種幹細胞治療 , 已經超過40年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年裡 , 骨髓幹細胞已經爆發了 , 用來治療病人的其他疾病 , 比如心臟疾病、血管疾病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經學上治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出來 , 我們商業化 , 今年 , 2.0名礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這會讓更多幹細胞被轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人參加潛在的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你可以禁止你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你比較年輕、更健康時 , 未來你就應該要用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們骨髓移植的倖存者 , 每年在史丹佛 , 聚集在一起 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪lisi提出一個有爭議的宇宙模型 , 可以回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有 , 它是你所見過最美麗的八度空間模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garrettlisi理論上 , 所有事情的理論都是如此 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 , 看看那些殺手方程式 。 真棒 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我會盡我所能地描述粒子物理的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭部都是一千個獨立的珊瑚礁 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚合物不斷地被灌溉並分成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	假如我們想像這是個超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨的個體 , 並問他一個很合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點中 , 和他的鄰居相比 , 如果只有機會 , 或命運 , 或要怎麼辦 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們大聲疾呼之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚的意思是 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤可以證明它 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚餐會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居非常清楚 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他同時也在所有其他地方 , 但在體驗它們的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分裂成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 超級聰明的珊瑚會特別準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常精確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們現實是不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們來說是很奇怪的一件事 , 因為我們只能體驗一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪的現象首先被erwinschringer和他的貓描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個組合中 , schrdinger是一個有放射性樣本的盒子 , 由量子力學定律 , 分成一個狀態 , 它的輻射和一個狀態 , 並不是 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本放射線的分支中 , 釋放毒藥和薛丁格死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一端 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個人之間 , 這些真實體驗都是獨立的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	到目前為止 , 另一個也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說是很奇怪的 , 因為我們每個人都經歷了個人的存在 , 而我們不見得會看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就好像我們每一個人 , 像schordinger一樣 , 都是一種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 這就是世界在小尺度上運作的樣子 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以在單一句子裡總結起來:所有事情都可能發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不代表一切發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理的其他部分是描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 每件事都是幾何學和基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	事情才會發生 , 只有這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述一下我們對這些粒子的認識 , 它們是什麼 , 以及它的平衡是如何運作的 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 一束質子和反質子被加速到接近光速 , 融合成碰撞 , 產生出一股純淨能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量會馬上轉換成海原粒子的噴泉 , 用探測器和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有17英里 , 當它在運作時 , 引發了五倍的力量 , 就像蒙特利的城市一樣 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法準確地預測哪些粒子會在任何個體碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理告訴我們 , 粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量相同於質子和反質子 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子都比這種能源限制還大 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這種新的粒子加速器非常令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越前所未有的能量限制七倍之外所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我描述我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一系列的亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	大部分的人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這間房間裡有很多人會把他們推過來 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中立的夥伴叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和一個非常微小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下方的夸克有很大的質量 , 三分之二 , 將質子和中子結合 , 讓原子在原子裡面 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都在左右 , 和右邊的種類 , 帶有相反的電荷的反粒子 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉 , 第三代 , 相同的載荷和第一代相同 , 但質量更高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些粒子都與各種力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過所謂的光子 , 電粒子互相作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	也有一種非常弱的力量 , 非常不想像力 , 很弱的力量 , 只有左手物質 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用帶有不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 帶有三種不同的種類:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 重力的力量 , 透過質量和旋轉來交互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一股力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量 , 根據每個粒子都有的相應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒見到的粒子 , 但我們很肯定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它給了其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎很確定它會發生 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎題是我們可能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我要給你們看一段美麗的可能性來到這場演說結束 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 。 這裡有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	這是很多粒子來追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	自然界中有很多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果根據他們的指控 , 就會出現一些美麗的圖案 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和下方的夸克結合成一個質子 , 它有完全的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷其實是另一組電荷的組合:超電荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超電荷和弱荷分開 , 將粒子的載荷放在這兩度電荷空間中 , 電荷會在垂直方向附近這些粒子 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力相互作用 , 根據它們的超電波和弱電荷 , 會產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 統一性的選舉模型 」 , 它在1967年被放回來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以只熟悉電荷 , 而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯有很大的質量 , 破壞了這個選舉模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會讓弱力變弱 , 讓弱粒子變得很弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這張圖表中巨大的希格斯會沿著水平方向沿著電磁共振成像的光子在電荷空間的垂直方向上維持著巨大的作用
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被二度空間載荷所描述的這個模式 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力的力量擴散出兩個載荷方向 , 將引導力帶到這些方向上 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中繪製並投射到像這樣的兩度空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子互動時 , 大自然就會在四個載荷方向上保持平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子碰撞 , 它會產生一股能量 , 以及四個載荷方向的零 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這一刻 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 維持零的總載量 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 控訴總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱粒子可以腐化成電子和反中子 , 這三個粒子依然加上零 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式不僅是漂亮的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 什麼互動被允許發生 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察這個強大的互動 , 它有這種很好的六角形對稱 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強大的互動中 , 強力粒子 , 例如這個 , 和有色的夸克互動 , 例如這個綠色的 , 用不同的顏色來配合這個紅色的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的交互作用每秒鐘發生在我們身體的每個原子核中數百萬次 , 把原子核包起來 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷相對應到三股力量 , 並不是故事的終點 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也能再加上兩個載荷來對應重力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們包含在一起 , 每一個粒子都有兩種不同的轉動載荷、轉動和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開 , 在六維充電空間中 , 提供一個很好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它是相當漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這種模式符合我們目前對大自然的最佳知識 , 以這些基本粒子的規模建造 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們對肯定的了解 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子的確極限於我們與實驗進行的範圍 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道這些微小的物理學 。 宇宙和這些微小的尺度是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些我們還不知道的新點子 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要單獨用數學來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把我們的手放在整個enchilada上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有的粒子和力量 , 來構成我們宇宙的完整照片 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測我們會看到的新粒子 , 當實驗達到更高能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 粒子物理學中有個舊的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從更完美的模式中出現 , 讓希格斯粒子斷裂 , 讓電磁力分裂 , 以提供電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子在這個方向上載荷 , 然後我們可以把粒子轉向另一個方向 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們就能建構標準載荷的六度空間 , 作為一個破壞的對稱 , 在七度空間中 , 這種完美的模式 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特定的選擇在1973年由pati和salam所提出的一個偉大的統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新統一的模式 , 我們可以看到一些落差 , 粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家會尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包括以下為基礎的建立模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這一組載荷 , 考慮一個奇怪的事實:第二和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是獨一無二的辨識出來的六個載荷 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的另一端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以將獨特的新載荷分配給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個模式是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質有關聯於第一個世代的對稱叫做 「 試驗 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中 , 這個特殊的載荷模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大例外的謊言團體 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的 , 曲線形狀是248度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個模式中 , 每一點都對應著這種非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦的廣義相對論 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	加上量子力學 , 這種形狀的幾何形狀可以描述宇宙在最小的尺度上如何運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的形狀在八度載荷空間中是非常美麗的 , 它將成千上萬的相互作用 , 結合了這些基本粒子之間的關係 , 每一個都是複雜的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	正如我們所旋轉的 , 我們可以看到其中許多其他複雜的圖形 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特殊的旋轉 , 我們可以從八度空間看下去 , 沿著對稱軸 , 同時看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 在那裡 , 新的粒子被這個模式所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	這裡有20個空隙 , 新粒子應該被派遣粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們的位置 , 我們知道這些新的粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的疤痕 , 但有顏色充電 , 和強力互動 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	在這些新的粒子中填滿了這個模式 , 給我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8模式有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	被認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這種偉大的數學美的物體可以描述粒子交互作用的真理 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然被數學所描述的概念並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這個: 「 大自然的孫子書 , 它不斷地打開我們的凝視 , 寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	牠的角色是三角形、圓圈和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有任何人類無法理解它的單一字 ; 沒有這些 , 一隻在黑暗的迷宮中揮舞 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著跟隨著伽利略的指引 , 描述粒子物理的數學 , 只用三角形、圓圈和其他幾何形的數字 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這些東西時 , 數學就能夠組成暗迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但在數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這個數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 隨著長長大的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個地方互動 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著圖案越來越多 , 用像大型強子對撞機的視角來看 , 我們或許可以看出大自然是不是使用這種e8模式或不同的形式 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這項發現的過程是一項很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8模式的粒子 , 那會非常非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現了新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對這個e8理論來說 , 不好意思 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說 , 不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那到底有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這理論和其它類似的照片 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個做過很多困難的工作 , 知道大部分的點子可能不會是對大自然的真理 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有大量的野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大投資一樣 , 可能會很難拋棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果沒有用的話 , 你就得要把它弄出來 , 嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 要維持公平和成就幸福的唯一方法 , 就是保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我竭盡所能地生活平衡生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我生活在物理、愛和衝浪之間的平衡 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	如此一來 , 即使我工作的物理都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過著好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年來 , 我都住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	宇宙中最偉大的謎題之一 , 是我父母 , 我如何能在沒有完整的職業中生存下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要讓你們看這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在maui的家裡辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能注意到這些美麗的景象很相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在梅伊的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心租金讓我花時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	活在遊牧者的存在是很困難的 , 但它讓我能活在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 我一生都很快樂 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花了很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概知道其中的百分之二 , 但我仍然很愛它 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的一切理論:我習慣於珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 。 至少有幾個人感到興奮是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會帶來重力和量子理論 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以你是說我們應該考慮宇宙 , 在它的核心中 , 最小的東西 , 是否有e8物件的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 是否有規模 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	蓋爾:嗯 , 現在我展示給你們看的圖案 , 和我們對基本粒子物理的認識有關 , 已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說的 , 我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有很大的相似性 , 以及它融入這個e8的圖案 , 可能是其餘的圖像 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我向你們展示的這些圖案 , 其實代表著這種高度維度的物體 , 會被扭曲、移動、和跳舞的對稱性 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就是我們所看到的所有元素粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論學家 , 如我所知 , 解釋電子 , 以較小的弦振動 , 我知道你不喜歡弦的理論 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該怎麼看待電子與e8的關係呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當形狀在空間中移動時 , 它會扭曲 。 當它移動時 , 它會扭曲它的方向 。 所以 , 克:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子是如何相連的 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它更大嗎 ? 它更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:就像我們所知的電子是指定的粒子 , 所以它會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以這些東西在量子場理論上被解釋 , 所有的可能性都在不斷擴張 , 同時發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我會用比喻來對珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的出現方式就是 , 每個時間點都附在一個形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說的 , 形狀扭曲了方向 , 隨著形狀扭轉 , 扭曲的表面是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 他們把自己當作點和互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能更清楚一點 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	我當然想要更了解這一點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常謝謝你來這裡 。 這絕對令人著迷 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究者珍•古拉爾談到計程車和其它社區專案 , 協助在非洲大城的居民 , 威脅動物 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古德勒能協助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 賈莫 , 吉他 , 邦諾 , 但是我們也可以啊 , 喔 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺之前所說的 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一個 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上我要跟大家分享我的演講 , 今天晚上 , 時間是零日離開的 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談這個奇妙、三歲的澳洲兒童 , 塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽說過歷史、家族樹 , 透過dna基因資料 , 人類的家族樹 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	那是一位古生物學家 , 最近的路易斯•路克伊 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時是非常不凡的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	它現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石的形狀 , 知道它們的外觀是什麼樣子 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 和它們所生活的各種物品的方式 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但 , 他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在是相當常見的理論 , 如果我們在我們最接近的活體親戚身上發現行為模式 , 或類似人類的行為模式 , 大約七百萬年前 , 人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把這些特徵從古代、古老的過去帶到我們身上 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看一下今天的教科書處理人類演化時 , 你常常會發現人們對人類的行為有多早 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比任何其他生物都更像我們在這場ted會議中所聽到的還要多 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以它仍然讓我在某些方面留下評論黑猩猩的評論 , 跟我們一樣 , 在某些方面 , 牠們的行為 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年 , 儘管我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外生存到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	華爾先生 , 雌性先生11或12歲 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五六年就只有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期以來的兒童依賴於生育 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 回到她身邊 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長期的童年對黑猩猩很重要 , 就如同我們和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同的動物演化過程中變得更複雜 , 所以我們發現學習在個人的生命史上扮演更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間看牠們的長輩會做些什麼 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道它們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式是 , 目前在所有不同的黑猩猩族群中 , 都已經在非洲研究過 , 透過觀察、模仿、實踐 , 來形容這些工具的行為是原始的文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有言語 。 我們談到這一點 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	它們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 許多都很相似 , 甚至相同 , 相同的 , 在相同的情境中 , 形成了黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也親吻雙手 , 手 , 拍另一張 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們會游動 , 牠們會丟石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多關於同情心的例子 , 前者會愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 他們的天性有黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們有能力極度殘酷 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些真的很積極的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常積極 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物 , 已經幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物界之間沒有線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們更加觀察 , 越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究仍然持續到現在 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 活在野外的複雜社交生活中 , 比任何其他事物都更有幫助 , 使我們意識到我們是其中的一部分 , 而非分離 , 和我們共享地球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很難找到黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是從空氣中拍攝的一張照片 , 它給你看gombe的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時我在整個領域飛越 , 大約十六年前 , 發現在公園外 , 這個森林 , 在1960年間 , 幾乎沒有破碎 , 沿著湖泊的海岸 , 那裡是小小的 , 30平方公園 , 那是我心中的問題 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何試著拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當住在全國公園附近的居民掙扎著生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比起土地 , 更多的居民都能支持土地 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民數目增加 , 來自於剛果湖泊的難民數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	窮人買不起其他食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這個計畫導致了我們稱之為 「 計程 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的方式來改善生活在公園附近的村民的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村落開始 , 現在是24個 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間可以進去 , 但包含樹木護士 , 目前為止最適合農業的方法 , 幾乎像沙漠的土地在這些山裡 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 預防土壤的侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	再利用過度使用的農地 , 這樣兩年內 , 他們就可以再次生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	要協助村民從井中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建立一些教室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群婦女合作 , 提供他們機會 , 提供微型貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們已經知道 , 世界各地有95%的貸款 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權婦女 , 和教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 這樣她們才能完成中學 , 清楚地了解到 , 全世界 , 女性的教育改善 , 家庭大小降低 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 關於保育 , 有些事情正在發生 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育正在發生的是 , 農夫住在這24個村落 , 而不是把我們視為一群白人 , 來研究一群猴子 , 順道一提 , 許多員工現在都是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始計程 , 坦尚尼亞的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞團隊和村民談話 , 詢問他們對什麼感興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間持續下去 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始對保育的需求越來越了解 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白 , 隨著山丘上升的層級被摧毀 , 所以你有可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展所謂的 「 大猩猩生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這裡是全國公園外的一個區域 , 延伸到這些非常低級的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村莊有更好的生命標準時 , 他們其實同意把百分之十到二十的土地放到高地上 , 再一次的 , 隨著樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩就會有葉窗的走廊 , 讓牠們可以在國家公園外的遺傳性團體互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 泰卡爾是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方複製它 , 圍繞著其他荒野地區 , 面對著極端的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們剛剛討論的前幾天 , 都是大問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮有很多 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你收到大量住在土地裡的人們 , 這不是肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍樹樹時 , 你把土壤留在空中 , 如同絕望的族群砍伐越來越多的樹木 , 所以他們可以試著為自己和家人種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定會發生什麼事 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	除了非洲 , 還有其它發展中國家的問題 , 實際上 , 到處都是我們對地球所做的事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 知名的科學家e.wilson說如果地球上每一個人都能維持平均歐洲或美國人的生活水準我們需要三個新的星球
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現今 , 他們說四個 。 但我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事呢 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 我們是最聰明的生物 , 最聰明的生物 , 帶著這種非凡的大腦 , 可以用這些ted會議來描述的科技 , 然而我們卻破壞了我們唯一的家 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大的決定之前 , 曾經坐下來問自己: 「 這個決定會如何影響我們的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 主要的決定 , 我並不是在這裡談非洲 , 而是發展中國家的主要決策 , 包括數百萬美金 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於 「 這會如何影響下一股股股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始環遊非洲談到黑猩猩和牠們的消失森林所面臨的問題時 , 我越來越了解到 , 許多非洲的問題可以在前殖民地開發的門口 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外旅行 , 在歐洲演講 , 和美國談話 , 來到亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我在說的那種話 。 我在談污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水可能是我們這個世紀所面臨的最關鍵問題之一 , 每個地方的水被農業、工業和家庭的化學物質污染 , 仍然遍及世界各地 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤的侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有不幸的燃燒化石燃料 , 還有其他溫室氣體 , 叫做 「 氣候變遷 」 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 世界各地 , 人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候有一些問題正在發生 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都被混合了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	窮人受到更糟的影響 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲許多地方 , 乾旱更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 它通常會導致洪水 , 加入痛苦 , 貧窮和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	居住在一個區域 , 土地無法支援 , 他們太貧窮 , 無法購買食物 , 因為整個土地被破壞了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的危機 , 火化 , 火化 , 當樹的最後一邊被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 而是全世界 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我並不意外 , 我遇見了這麼多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	各位認為 , 這種非凡聰明的大腦可能有某種差異 , 像是ted科技 , 人類心臟 ? 在非科學的角度 , 以愛和同理心來說 , 是否有某種差異 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們是憂鬱、悲傷 , 或生氣 。 他們說了更多或多或少 , 說: 「 我們有這種感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 且我們無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我想我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 從我年紀開始 , 我感覺到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這項計畫導致了我們稱之為根和芽 , 此計畫始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在散播到世界各地九十七個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根建立了一間公司基金會 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎很小 , 要到達太陽 , 才能打破磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為我們在地球上遇到的所有問題 , 環保和社會問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地有數十萬名年輕人可以打破 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根和芽的重要訊息:我們每個人每天都能有所改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每個人 , 我們都有選擇 , 我們想要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 , 要我們改變事物 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根和芽團體都選擇了三個專案 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於它們的年齡 , 而這個國家 , 不論它們在城市或鄉村 , 都取決於什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有來自學齡前學院的方案 , 越來越多的成人開始屬於他們自己的根和芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體都選擇 , 在他們之間 , 三個不同的項目 , 來讓這個更美好的世界 , 認知到這些不同的問題都是互相連結 , 並且互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一項計畫是協助他們自己的族群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	如果他們能做到 , 他們可能會募到資金來幫助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是協助動物 , 不僅是野生動物 , 家庭的動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一項計畫是幫助我們分享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切中 , 沃文是一種學習在和平和諧中生活的訊息 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區中 , 在國家、文化、宗教之間 , 和我們之間的信仰之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們無法以我們速度摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個地球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要在非洲這裡挑出一兩項項項項目:根和芽團體正在做 , 只有在坦尚尼亞 , 在肯亞 , 南非 , 剛果 , 獅子山共和國 , 攝影機 , 還有其他團體 。 如我所說 , 它是在世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們正在種樹 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 有雞和雞蛋 , 只用一點點的錢 , 或用它們來餵飽他們的家人 , 並感受到驕傲和賦權 , 因為他們不再有幫助 , 依靠其它的蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理協助給予士兵 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	像這樣做 , 把他們自己帶出去 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	同樣的 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們也在監獄裡也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多的根和芽的時間 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根和芽的重要元素 , 隨著年長的孩子和年輕的孩子談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	那些沒有預期的懷孕和類似的事情 , 年輕人聽得更好 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過太多可怕的東西 , 你看過你的黑猩猩數從一百萬 , 到現在 , 沒有超過十五萬隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 一旦有森林 , 沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 對吧 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是令人驚訝的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我一直很興奮 , 最後 , 來到人們談到作曲線 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們就把這些水沖到水道上 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到再生能源極度重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否關心孩子的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩或孫子 , 姪子 , 姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否在乎他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以選擇我們每天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買了什麼 。 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用這個問題來做選擇 , 會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他長大後 , 會如何影響我的孩子 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或其它的 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心相處 , 我們加入世界各地 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	而這正是ted的幫助 , google幫助我們 , 埃斯里也幫助我們 , 幫助我們在gombe國家公園裡繪圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你們已經聽說過這次下午 。 開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這改變了 , 這改變了 。 看看我們在乎未來的改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由是驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以拿一個完全被摧毀的區域 , 隨時間而來 , 也許有一些幫助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	一個例子是計程車計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你們 , 看似死掉的樹木會不會因為木頭而被駭 , 而你不用再因為你有木頭 , 五年之內就可以有三十英呎的樹木 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	幾乎在絕種的邊緣上 , 動物可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它很有啟發性 。 它帶我到我最後的希望類別 , 我們在過去兩天聽到了這麼多:這種無形的人類精神 。 這種人類精神的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 這樣你會認為會被貧窮、疾病所擊垮 , 或不管怎樣 , 有時候可以用幫助手 , 把他們帶到社會中 , 把他們的一部分帶到改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想非洲有一兩個人 , 他們真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但顯然是尼爾森•曼德拉 , 從17年的硬體勞工 , 23年的監禁 , 讓他能帶領他的國家在沒有血腥的惡魔政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 在奈及利亞 , 他採用了巨型石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都盡力執行 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人非常鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是非洲年輕人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天也聽到了其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	我真的很感激這個機會能再次分享這個訊息 , 讓ted的每個人 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人可以聚集在一起 , 談論這些事 , 特別是根和芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個字是 , 跑完這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 用她的證據 , 她是根和芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達瑞薩拉姆的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說 , 這協助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我很興奮能見到她 , 看看年輕人如何被賦予權力 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家戴安娜•柯恩分享了一些關於塑膠污染的真理 , 關於我們生活中的塑膠污染 , 以及一些想法 , 如何將我們自己從塑膠灰色中解放 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜.柯恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是個視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 在過去的20年 , 我剪斷和縫紉在一起 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩個三度空間的碎片、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	和塑膠一起工作 , 大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始融化 , 分解成較小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	教育我自己對塑膠有更深的了解 , 我發現這是一件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成小塊 , 因為它總是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們所發現的是 , 海洋環境中有很多 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾堆和蓋瑞 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應 , 我認為這是很多人對它的反應: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須去那裡清理這東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	因此我開發了一個提案 , 用一艘貨船和兩艘退化的捕魚拖車 , 一輛拖車 , 一台拖車 , 一台冷卻機和一台冷卻的機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是去健身房 , 提高這個議題的認知 , 開始將塑膠切片切成小塊 , 冷卻的磚塊 , 可能被用來當作隱藏社區的材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和實際去過健身房的人談談 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 並且在做這件事 , 我意識到 , 要把它們清理 , 要和全世界每天所產生的垃圾相比 , 實際上 , 我需要回頭看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的圖片是:我們需要找到一個方法來關閉偽裝 。
