we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切割單一和可避免的塑膠的位置 , 每天進入海洋環境的位置 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	因此 , 我也了解到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 在太平洋的海洋中 , 我學到現在有11個環節 , 可能是世界上五個主要海洋中的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我不只關心塑膠的健身 , 超市裡的塑膠健身 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都包含在塑膠裡 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我的所有平均都是塑膠包裝 , 甚至是健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也擔心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我擔心塑膠和從塑膠帶到我們體內的毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人一起研究這個問題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多倡議 , 我們正在努力 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	一是:如果我們在海洋中發現的百分之八十至九十--我們在海洋中發現的海洋是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不稱之為它是什麼 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收所有人的書籍 , 都是關於能永續且環保的 , 和回收的概念有關 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把某樣東西放進一圈 , 你不用再想一想 。
what is the reality of that ?	現實的真相是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 不到7%的塑膠回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的仔細觀察 , 尤其當談到塑膠瓶時 , 大部份只會被降低或內在 , 或是運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降低 , 變成更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 或是再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們看到的另一件事是 , 請大家思考一下 , 我們把第四個r加在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 前面 , 「 三個r , 拒絕了 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	不論何時 , 都拒絕使用單一和可用的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是很古老的學者 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 使用這些裝置 , 而不是放大和upware的容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易撿起一瓶無棍的瓶子 , 或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 且你忘記要把你的不穩定的瓶子裡裝滿水 , 或過濾水 , 對抗塑膠瓶水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想跟大家說的 , 我知道你們都知道這個議題 , 是因為這在海洋中是個很大的問題 , 但這是我們作為消費者所創造的一個問題 , 我們可以解決這個問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高警覺 , 來解決這個問題 , 來教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 無論何時 , 選擇用單一塑膠替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把幹細胞綁在我們的海洋中 , 這樣做 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	麻省理工學院的帕特•馬斯的實驗室主張 , 普拉夫•帕特利是ted的buz 。 它是一個可穿戴的裝置 , 用來對環境的深刻互動 。 想像一下 「 少數 」 和一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	demo , 設計 , 介面設計 , 科技 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattimaes和pranav密碼示範第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很感興趣 , 是否能演化或發展第六種感官 , 能讓我們無縫的接觸、容易取得代謝或信息 , 來協助我們做出正確的決策 , 來協助我們做出正確的決策 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們當中有些人可能會說 , 嗯 , 今天的手機是否已經做到了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說 , 不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted這裡見到某人 , 當然是最頂尖的網路場所 , 你不會搖動某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能在我拿出手機 , 谷歌搜尋你嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或當你去超市你站在那大型的衛生紙上你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 然後去一個網站試著判斷哪些不同的衛生紙是最環保的購買中心 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有容易取得相關的資訊 , 能協助我們做出最佳決定 , 決定下一步要做什麼 , 以及採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 以一種簡單的方式 , 不用要求使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭開我們最新的努力 , 到目前為止 , 這仍是非常成功的過程 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在正穿著這個裝置 , 我們將它和架子上的零件組合在一起 , 順便說一下 , 當時的成本只有350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我穿著一個相機 , 一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式的電池投影系統 , 一個小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡交流到我的手機裡 , 它扮演了通訊和運算裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在這段影片中 , 我們看到我的學生普拉夫•帕特利 , 他真的是執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們可以看到這個系統讓他走向任何表面 , 開始使用他的手 , 來和他前面投影的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤四個手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他穿著很簡單的標記帽子 , 讓你知道 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更具體的版本 , 你也可以用不同的顏色畫出你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上會追蹤這四個手指 , 並且辨識出他製造的任何姿勢 , 例如 , 長灘的地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也認出 「 拍照 」 的標誌姿勢 , 然後拍一張照片 , 不論在你面前是什麼 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他回到媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何牆上 , 投影他所拍攝的所有照片 , 把它們整理起來 , 再次用自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 兩年前有些人可能在場 , 看到jefhan或有些人可能會想: 「 嗯 , 這看起來不像微軟表面桌嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的姿勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但差別在於 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西是可用的 , 和這個專案資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 一個重要的差異是 , 它完全是行動 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差異是 , 在大規模生產中 , 明天不會比現在的手機還要多 , 實際上 , 比我在脖子上穿的版本還要多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除此之外 , 讓你們當中的一些人比如在《少數民族報告》裡的tomruise , 我們對於這個裝置的理由是它真的可以作為這六感的裝置之一 , 讓你知道你面前的任何資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕拉病毒進入超市 , 他正在購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品 , 系統就能辨識出他撿起的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠光或橘色光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以請求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特定的選擇是特別好的選擇 , 因為他的個人特質 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能會想要有廁所的紙 , 而不是最能負責任的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡撿起一本書 , 他就可以拿到亞馬遜評分 , 它就會被投射在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們先前的講者 , 順便說一下 , 亞馬遜的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , pranav轉變了這本書的頁面 , 可以看到書的讀者評論 , 可能是他最喜歡的評論信 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉向一個特定的頁面 , 他可能會找到一個朋友的註解 , 給他一點額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何事 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙永遠不需要太過時了 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以收到你閱讀的影片註冊 , 你可以得到最新的運動分數 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是一個更具爭議性的 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某個人互動 , 也許你會看到一個標籤的字 , 和那個人的部落格和個人網頁的連結 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生感興趣的是攝影機等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你到機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的飛行延遲 , 閘門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道當下的時光 , 就如同在手臂上繪圖一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	到目前為止 , 我們正在發展第六種感官 , 讓我們無縫取得這些相關的資訊 , 來了解我們可能碰到的事物 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生普拉夫 , 真的很像我說的 , 背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確值得很多掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去三個月內睡覺 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也不太開心 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但這還不完美 , 進步很多 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許在接下來的十年 , 我們會來到這裡 , 最終的第六感腦植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	2001年9月11日 , 菲爾德里茲和艾瑞克•瓦菲有一個強大的友誼 , 來自世界貿易中心的兒子被殺害 , 在2001年9月11日 , 艾爾瓦菲的兒子桑卡索瓦烏烏烏爾被告知在那些攻擊中扮演的角色 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩位媽媽已經開始了解彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治議題、政治議題、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11療癒:找到寬恕、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲莉絲•羅德里格茲:我們今天在這裡 , 是因為我們大部分人認為是不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	可是 , 我們現在感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次學到我兒子在2001年9月11日的交易中心 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他在36小時後還沒死掉 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會用我兒子的名字來命名 , 奧蘭多和我的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 經過震驚 , 驚恐的震驚 , 和我們生活中的糟糕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們並沒有被感動 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後 , 當zacariasmoussaoui被指控為犯下恐怖主義 , 而美國政府為他打電話給死刑 , 如果定罪 , 我的丈夫和我公開對話 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些 , 透過人權團體 , 我們和許多其他受害者的家庭聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha時 , 她兒子被指控出來 , 我心想: 「 勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要見到那位女子 , 我更強壯 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在悲傷中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或者我們會找到對方 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我立即得到同理心 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被指控的是什麼時 , 她並沒有得到同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , aicha現在會告訴你這如何發生 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安各位先生女士
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmosaoui的媽媽 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我詢問了人權組織讓我聯絡受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹了我五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我受苦很多 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 我十六歲時 , 第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , zacaria的故事實在太大了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然痛苦 , 因為我的兒子就像被埋葬了 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否活著 , 我不知道他有被折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 所以 , 我的苦難對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對於所有給予生命的女人 , 所有的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	我們是女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須有手工 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是對女人、對我們女人、對我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年輕的穆斯林女孩談話 , 所以她們不接受和她們的意志結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 避免她們和我一樣結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是我站在你們面前的原因 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	帕特:我想說 , 我從aicha學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們和其他家庭成員第一次見面 , 那是一個非常私人的會議 , 因為這是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時的美國成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都很緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 為什麼她想要見我們 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們要見她 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們彼此想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們認識他人的名字之前 , 或任何東西之前 , 我們已經擁抱和wept 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們在一個充滿支持的圈子裡 , 協助 , 從人們體驗到這種解析 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子有罪 , 或無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我對你的家庭發生了什麼事有多抱歉 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道要受苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果犯罪 , 一個人應該被公平地懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那樣的方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想要說 , 那是個冰箱 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都告訴我們的故事 , 我們都與人類連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	到了下午的結束 , 午餐三小時後 , 我們覺得好像彼此認識了 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是女性 , 不僅僅是她在這些現況下慷慨地慷慨 , 還有她兒子的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼艱難的人生 , 從這樣的文化和環境中 , 遇到過一個人 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有很特別的關聯 , 我很重視 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我覺得這一切都要害怕別人 , 但要讓這一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這實在太難了 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能碰到我不知道的 , 或我和誰不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說 , 我們必須試著認識他人 , 另一個人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要慷慨 , 你的心一定要慷慨 , 你的心一定要慷慨 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要忍受 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天我們都能同心協力 , 彼此尊重 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這就是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多人無法取得乾淨飲用水 。 工程師麥可•普萊卡做了點什麼 , 發明了可攜式的生物濾鏡 , 可以在二零九年 , 讓水飲用量最多 。 一個來自tedglobal的美妙的展示 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、demo、設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水、水 。
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	michaelprichard的水過濾器變成有用的水是可以飲用的 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談一些事情 。
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都在享受這邊為你們提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它來自這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	統計數據會說 , 你們當中一半的人會遭受腹瀉的痛苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我談過很多關於統計數據 , 以及所有人飲用水的建設 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎沒有通過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經知道為什麼了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 利用目前的思維 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就關掉:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想用不同的思考方式來告訴各位 , 這個問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順便說一下 , 自從我說起 , 全世界有一萬三千人遭受痢疾 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛過世了 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了救生素瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的一天 , 當我看著亞洲海嘯的消息 , 滾動在電視上 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週、幾週 , 人們逃到山丘 , 被迫飲用污染的水或面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的困擾著我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	幾個月後 , 颶風卡崔娜衝進了美國 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道 , 要花五天才能讓水到超級迷宮嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上射擊電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	我在車庫裡花了很多時間 , 在接下來的幾週和幾個月 , 我廚房裡也對我妻子感到不安 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在少數失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , 救命的瓶子 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在來談談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在生命saver之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以200奈米的細菌會穿過200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這絕對會穿過這兩百奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生命沙龍是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 什麼都沒有 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我要給你們一些示範 。
would you like to see that ?	你想要看到嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間設定出來 , 所以我猜我應該這樣做 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在牛津城 。
so someone's done that up .	所以 , 有人這麼做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	牛津的城市 , 我已經離開了 , 把一些水從河流cherwell和河水流過來 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我想 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中間 , 水就不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我已經去了 , 加入一些東西 。
and this is from my pond .	這是我池塘 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	請聞一下 , 攝影師的氣味
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們要把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelprichard:好的 , 我們有一些從污水農場跑出來的 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以我要把它放進去 。
put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 , 就這樣 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	另外一些小片段和碎片 , 把它切下來 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我有個朋友的兔子的禮物 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	所以 , 我們也要把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	救生素瓶真的很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水堆起來 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用果汁給你們看 , 讓你們看一下裡面的小孔 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這還不夠髒 , 先稍微站一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我要把這個非常骯髒的水放在這裡 , 你想要喝嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好 , 我們開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給你幾個幫浦 , 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把脂肪抽出來 , 蒸汽飲用水就會出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得很快就準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	來了 。 請注意電力 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全、穩定的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯在其他節目裡的程式 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的 。 全世界數以千計的人都使用過生命瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會維持六千公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它爆炸時 , 使用失敗的科技 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把卡路里趕出去 , 打個新的 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	對另一萬六千公升來說是好事 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	接著 , 幾週後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進入營地 , 取得他們的安全飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地時會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病散播 , 需要更多資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就變成了自我繁殖 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的方式思考 , 運送這些資料 , 人們可以留下來 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以製造自己的穩定飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要自然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	使用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道是太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上執行數字時 , 你就會出錯 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這裡是 「 思考 」 的位置 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	取而代之 , 用手工程來處理它 , 讓我們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡拿起水 , 免費送到那裡 , 把水送到山上 , 河流 , 溪流 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們所要做的就是讓它穩定 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以使用生物水瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以用其中一種 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 用噴射機就能做到 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理二萬五千公升的水 ; 足夠四個家庭 , 三年之久 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	一天大約半美金 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 處理水的過程 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四個小時 , 才能取得他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	它們可以從附近的來源 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要花了八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧年目標 , 來拯救人們的數量 , 不用取得安全飲用水 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	要把它放入國外援助的情況下 , 美國政府每年花費大約120億英鎊 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以每年有三千五億人遭受痛苦 , 每年有兩百萬名孩童死於死亡 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyshdown聲稱我們生活在歷史上 , 權力在從未有過的方式改變 。 在tedxbrusel的演講中 , 他提出了三項重大的全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化、文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyshdown:全球的權力轉變 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩寫作是十九世紀末有著名的英文詩人 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 它被用來回應教會的大腦 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩說: " 在夏天的大山上 , 帶著蒸汽的流動 , 哈克我聽到一個遙遠的鼓聲 , 像夢裡的聲音 , 很近、很低、很大聲 , 在地球的路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物來粉絲、士兵遊行 , 很快就死了 。 "
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩歌感興趣的人 , 詩是 " 由a.e.sman所寫的 " shropshirelad " 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但housman也知道 , 在尼爾森的交響樂中 , 你也聽到它 , 那就是 , 十九世紀的長期 , 溫度、溫度、溫溫度的夏天即將進入一個接近的時代 , 我們即將進入歷史的恐怖時期 , 當權力改變 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	女士們先生們 , 這些都是經常出現的 , 都伴隨著渦輪 , 血液也常常出現 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	而我的訊息是 , 我相信我們都被認為是肯定的 , 如果你喜歡 , 生活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當最高階的權力開始改變 , 世界的新角度 , 存在的新勢力開始開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些都是現在我們很清楚的看到 , 幾乎永遠都很亂、很困難的時刻 , 都太累了 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便說一下 , 每一世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會主張 , 最後一次發生了 , 那就是霍斯曼的感受 , 以及教會的感受 , 當權力通過舊國 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 橫跨大西洋 , 到美國新興的新興力量開始時 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 當時歐盟的權力是過去一世紀的兩場血腥災難 , 第二部分是:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	maozedong曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天要談三種因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 這兩者是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二 , 關於一些新的維度 , 我想要介紹 , 這從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談在世界發生權力的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的狀況是 , 在某種意義上 , 嚇到是因為從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到了革命性的權力轉變為羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明期間發生的權力轉變 , 但我們看到一些稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅僅是從國家到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也在垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今正在發生的是 , 負責責責任的權力 , 在國家國家的制度中 , 已經遷移到全球階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力 , 我們談的是市場化 , 但實際上是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級上 , 權力被告知權力是法律制定的 , 在國際舞台上 , 這不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台現在的權力是:網際網路的力量 , 衛星廣播公司的權力 , 金錢會改變這廣大的金錢演算法 , 現在是32倍 , 交易所必要的金錢 , 應該是有資金改變者 , 如果你喜歡 , 財務演算家 , 把我們帶到我們的膝蓋裡 , 近期 , 跨國企業的權力 , 經常會發展出比起大的國家還要大 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球空間裡 , 大部分都沒有受到規範 , 不受法律規則的限制 , 人們可以自由地行動 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	那就適應了當下的力量 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合在沒有限制的空間中運作最多的人 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 不久後 , 沒有規範的空間 , 不受法律規則所影響 , 不單單單單是你想要國際貿易、網路等等 。 還有那些你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的事物 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的啟示是即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 空間能攻擊你 , 即使在你最典型的城市中 , 一個九月的早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 400萬美金中大約60%的資金被帶到911/11的資金中 , 通過了雙胞胎塔的機構 , 911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也使用這個空間 , 質量旅行、網路、衛星廣播 , 能夠繞過它們的毒物 , 目的是摧毀我們的系統和我們的方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久後 , 不久後 , 歷史的規則是權力的管理必須遵循 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 正如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象是全球化的力量 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰就是把治理帶到全球空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的數十年將會是更大、更大、更少的亂流 , 使我們能夠達成目標:把治理帶到全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在談建立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順便說一下 , 我自己的觀點 , 女士們先生女士們 , 這種觀點是不太可能發生的 , 透過擴展更多的聯合國制度 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種方式 , 讓你可以合法化的國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到全球空間的治理時 , 我猜這不會發生在美國創造出更多的聯合國機構 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 由強大的力量團結在一起 , 建立合約的系統、合法的協議、治理全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以治療為基礎的組織 , 完全是以治療的組織 , 然而 , 強大的力量 , 甚至連美國 , 如果需要的話 , 都會負責 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:努力奮鬥的開始 , 要建立一個合約的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道 , 我們必須組建一個機構 , 可以把治理帶到財務空間 , 來推測財務上的猜測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而g20就是以治療為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等一下會再回來談談 , 那就是如果你把最強大的力量集合起來 , 以合約的制度為基礎的制度 , 來填補那個治理空間 , 那麼 , 剩下的弱點會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 只要一秒鐘就回來了 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你通過這些亂流的次數 , 或更少的次數 , 那麼我們的成功會取決於我們的能力 , 來為全球空間帶來可信的治理 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這開始發生了 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談談 , 權力不僅僅是垂直轉變 , 它也在地平地轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會主張 , 文明史 , 文明的歷史一直都在海中聚集 , 和地中最早的居民聚集在一起 , 近期在西方國家的權力 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 我們現在看到的是一個重大的權力轉移 , 廣泛的說話 , 遠離大西洋環繞大西洋的國家 , 到太平洋的邊緣聚集在一起 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	從經濟力量開始 , 但這總是開始 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他種植權力的發展 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我覺得這不是西方世界的轉變 ; 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得的 , 美國在接下來的十年 , 將仍然是地球上最強大的國家 , 但她握有自己的權力 , 現在已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們從50年以來 , 最不尋常的歷史中 , 我們有一個完全獨立的世界 , 每一個羅盤 , 或反對 , 都必須被華盛頓的立場所參考 , 一個世界最好的一群人 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是更正常的歷史 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多點世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主要特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	它們仍然是最強大的國家 , 但它們將會是越來越多世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到中國的另一種權力中心 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜測是 , 中國和偉大無關 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	隨著中國開始民主化她的社會 , 自由化了她的經濟 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是個不同的討論主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度、巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到現在世界對歐洲人來說看起來更像是19世紀的歐洲
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在19世紀 , 一個偉大的英國外交部長 , 坎特 , 以前用來描述它是《歐洲音樂會》 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有平衡 , 五分之一的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是在平衡上演 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國和維也納及羅馬一起合作 , 提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個單一世界統治的時期 , 你已經修復了雙方聯盟 , 戰役的先鋒 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的權力的極端代表固定的盟友 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但權力的多極限意味著改變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們進入的世界 , 我們越來越會看到我們的聯盟不是固定的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	大英國外交部長曾說: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們越來越會看到即使我們在西方國家也必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋力量的結盟 , 如果我們想要在世界上做事 , 就能和他人聯盟 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們到利比亞 , 光是西方就不夠好了 , 我們就得帶其他人去 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須帶到阿拉伯聯盟 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗的最後一次 , 西方試圖自己做這件事 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我想我們已經到了400年的末期開始 , 我說了400年 , 因為那是西方國家權力的邊緣帝國 , 西方機構和西方價值觀的終止 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以向全世界的每個角落提出和消失 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是真的了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的最後一次財務危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金解決問題 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須呼籲他人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方的朋友圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你們做一個預測 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜我們現在已經到了400年的末 , 西方國家的權力足夠 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會涉及到和平、多邊和平 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔 , 沒錯 ? 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷底下 , 在藍色旗幟下 , 在聯合國指令下 , 服務全世界的國家 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一歲 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	何謂索馬利海盜的最佳航空聯盟 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的午餐內容 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是農民主義者 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要保持海道 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們要和我們不分享價值的人做生意 , 但隨著時間 , 我們有共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看世界 , 現在正在崛起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們現代的世界 , 是因為網路 , 因為人們在談論的這些事 , 一切都和一切有關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被關起來 , 作為一個國家 , 作為個體 , 在以前從未發生過的情況下 , 從未發生過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家的相互關聯 , 總是存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交的重點在於管理國家的關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被關起來了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到流感 , 那是24小時後 , 查爾斯•高爾機場的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降 , 很多崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯、非洲的食物暴動中 , 有火 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都非常、非常、非常、非常緊密的連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著一個國家單獨行動的概念 , 而不是與他人聯繫 , 不再是與他人合作 , 也不再是可行的提議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	由於國家國家的行為本身也不受限制 , 不對國家本身來控制它自己的領土 , 因為國外的影響已經開始影響它們內部的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一場小型帝國戰爭的士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的防禦是一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍有多強壯 , 我們的海軍有多強壯 , 以及我們的盟友有多強壯 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	敵人就在牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人就在牆裡 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談我國家的防禦 , 我必須和醫療部長談 , 因為流行疾病對我的安全有威脅 , 我必須和農業部談談 , 因為食物安全是對我的安全的威脅 , 我必須和工業部談談 , 因為我們的希臘基礎建設的脆弱 , 對於我們看到的敵人 , 我們的敵人 , 我必須對國內戰爭的威脅 , 談 , 我必須和國內的婦女談話 , 談談談 , 因為他們進入我國內的家裡 , 影響力 , 影響到我國內 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是國家安全的案例 , 只是對士兵和國防部的重要性 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力是將它的機構封鎖在一起 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直地建構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直的階層 , 專門處理任務 , 指令結構完全是錯誤的 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業界知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	網絡很重要 , 不論是在你的政府或外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這裡是阿什德丹的第三條法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 不要問我第一條法律和第二條法律 , 因為我還沒有發明出來 ; 如果第三條法則是比較好的 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三法則是 , 在現代的時代 , 每件事都與一切有關 , 最重要的是你能做的是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 你的結構不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊註冊 , 不論你是生意 , 你的交錯點 , 你和他人建立連結的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白在產業界 , 政府沒有 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事情 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 女士們先生們 , 我們現在被鎖在一起 , 用以前從來沒有完全相同的方式 , 那也是我們彼此的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體防禦 , 把我們當作保障國家的概念 , 已經不再夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的聯盟 , 像娜托 , 比他們的聯盟更強大 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是這樣 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互連結的出現 , 以及大規模毀滅的武器 , 意味著越來越多 , 我和我的敵人分享了命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	我當時是一位外交官協商在1970年代在日內瓦的蘇聯協商時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們共享的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩方都知道零和的遊戲是行不通的 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人分享了命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的最大障礙之一 , 就是 , 以色列 , 以及巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們有集體的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士 , 一直以來 , 遠見和詩人的提議變成了我們必須認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我會用一首詩來結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐恩的偉大詩
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要寄錢給誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是島嶼 。 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 為了我參與人類 , 我會被送去尋求誰的肚子 , 給誰的肚子 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰•唐恩來說 , 是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽的生活和健康的路徑 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 他們的長輩和vim和vigor一起生活 , 在tedxtc上 , 他分享了9個常見飲食和生活習慣 , 讓牠們能活到一百歲 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、科學、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到一百個+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一個名為丹麥雙胞胎研究指出 , 平均壽命的百分之十 , 在某些生物限制下 , 只有我們的基因被獨裁出來 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外90%則是我們生活方式的獨裁 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區域的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能找到一個事實證明的公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人長壽的最佳公式 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食 , 或墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品藥物管理局 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們什麼 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們什麼 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正能幫助我們活得更久 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是吃豆子嗎 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當談到供應時 , 你應該服用它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或反轉荷爾蒙呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是什麼 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法是與國家地理學會合作 , 國家老化學院合作 , 找出四個人口統一的區域 , 確認地理上的定義 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 帶一組專家到那裡 , 以正常的方式來處理這些人的做法 , 來分析跨文化分裂 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴你們哪些分裂 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要在長壽時破壞一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很難活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有5000人中只有1/100 。
your chances are very low .	你的可能性非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國成長最快的人口統計 , 很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們沒有長壽的程式設計 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們是為所謂的 「 積極成功 」 設計的 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 成功 」 , 意思是 , 你有孩子 , 再另一個世代 , 你的孩子有孩子時 , 年齡就會成功 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是一隻老鼠 , 或一隻大象 , 在中間 , 它是同一個故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	為了讓它變到一百歲 , 你不需要有很好的生活方式 , 你也得得到遺傳的彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療方法可以幫助緩慢、逆轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	僅僅幾分鐘 , 腦細胞就死了 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 毀掉你的軟骨 , 從來沒有回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊刺激 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆兆個細胞 , 上兆兆個 「 t 」 , 我們在這裡談的是國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年就會一次轉變一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們轉身時 , 就會產生一些損害 。 損害就會被破壞 。
and it builds up exponentially .	以指數的方式來建造 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像日子 , 當我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯時 , 我們會在casette錄音帶上複製 , 讓我們的朋友複製膠帶 , 很快地 , 帶著成功的世代 , 聽起來像是垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化速度比12歲的人快125倍
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有什麼能減緩你的老化或阻止你的老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 大約是90年 , 對女性來說 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家 , 平均壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線上 , 我們留下了12年的美好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些都是我們能得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究指出 , 大部分的疾病是慢性疾病、心臟疾病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的方法就是去看世界各地的文化 , 去體驗它們 , 在那裡 , 人們活到一百歲 , 比我們多出十倍 , 預期壽命是額外的幾十多年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸找到了第一座藍色區域 , 位於薩丁尼亞島 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做nuoro省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 男性生活最長的地區 , 大約是美國有10倍之多 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只到一百歲 , 他們就這樣做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	那裡有102歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 凝土木 , 比起他們還年輕60歲 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實回到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它實際上是一個被隔離的銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的不足 , 大多是牧羊 , 偶爾會是低密度的實體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	牠們的飲食主要是植物 , 牠們能帶到田野的食物集中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一支未發酵的麥田 , 叫做carta音樂 , 由鴨麥田製作的一種乳酪 , 由草食動物組成 , 乳酪是omega-3脂肪酸 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何已知葡萄酒都多了三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最出色的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲的時候達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 你得到越多的平等 , 越多的智慧就被讚頌 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你去薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 而不是看到運動顯示的游泳日曆 , 你看到月曆的百歲 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 老年人的父母不只能讓他們和家人保持密切關係 , 大約四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 對於那些家庭的孩子 , 死亡率較低 , 死亡率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一側發現了第二個藍色區域 , 大約800英哩的東京 , 位在奧克蘭哥的阿基比拉 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa實際上是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主要島嶼的北部 , 這是世界長壽的基礎 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是最古老的女性族群被發現的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	它是一個人們擁有世界上最長壽的地區 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活很長一段時間 , 牠們的睡眠很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 性行為之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命比一般美國人多七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍之多 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的殖民地和乳癌的比例 , 美國的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的機率是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化已經有了這些數字 , 建議他們有能力教我們一些東西 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次地 , 一個以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	和美國人一樣吃大約八倍的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更重要的是他們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的策略 , 來避免過渡期 , 如你所知 , 在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們會從小盤子裡吃掉 , 所以它們會在每一處吃少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 不如你在說話時 , 你可以無心地吃東西 , 給予對手的食物 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有3000年的廣告 , 我認為這是史上最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混亂所發明 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	飲食就是所謂的哈拉、哈特、哈特、布雷特 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在他們的餐點前提醒他們不要再吃掉他們80%的胃 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花大約半小時才能從腹部傳到腦部 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住 , 要阻止百分之八十的情況 , 它能幫助你不去做那件事情 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞 , okinawa有一些社會建構 , 讓我們能與長壽聯繫 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在就降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運地出生在俄亥俄州的奧庫瓦 , 你生來就有一套系統 , 裡面有一半的朋友 , 和你經歷過人生 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你在moai , 如果你遇到運氣時 , 就會有機會分享警訊 , 如果不好 , 孩子生病 , 家長死去 , 你總是有人有你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特別的moai , 這五位女士已經聚集了九十七年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成年生活分為兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 這對簡單的椅子也意味著退休 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在俄語中 , 甚至沒有退休的詞彙 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 一生中有一個詞 , 就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約翻譯的意思是 「 你早上醒來的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	在這位102歲的凱特大師 , 他的ikigai正帶著這種武術的藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	在這一百歲的漁夫 , 牠一直持續捕魚牠的家人三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所實際上給了我們一個問卷 , 給了這些百歲的人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們的文化非常地直覺 , 把問題問世的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	在這102歲的老婦人中 , 她的伊基吉格女子只是她的曾曾曾曾祖父 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲時分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著曾曾曾曾祖父的感覺是什麼感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回頭說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理學院的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們在明尼蘇達的展覽上看 , 實際上 , 有非常多的比例 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口 , 位在加州的七天廣告裡 , 集中在加州的羅馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	傳統主義者是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五晚上慶祝他們的安息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 24小時聖誕老人 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳遞給他們非凡的長遠習慣 , 比較像是說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的平均壽命是八十歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對於一位傳統主義者來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	不同之處在於 , 比起他們的美國對象 , 他們預期壽命約十一歲 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 我認為它馬上就說明了這個藍色區域的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異常的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共通點 , 是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 以至於他們大部分的人生習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經拿到飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	遺傳基因:1、29 , 上帝會談到遺體和種子 , 另一種則是關於綠色植物 , 卻忽略了肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們很認真地認真看待這一切 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週要花24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 他們在工作上有多緊張 , 孩子需要被驅動 , 他們阻止一切 , 他們專注於上帝、社交網路 , 接著 , 在宗教上 , 硬線是自然的走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這項技術的力量並不是偶爾完成的 , 電力是每一週完成的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有錢 , 沒有錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向於和其他的冒險家結合 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去看一位普通主義者的派對 , 你不會看到人們在搖滾jimbeam或搖滾一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談論下個自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻且可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這種文化已經產出值得讚揚的埃爾•沃雷罕 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯•沃爾罕是97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是多百萬富翁 , 但當承包商想要6 , 000美金來建造隱私的柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了我自己所付出的錢 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他在外面購買水泥 , 拖著兩極 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預測 , 也許 , 在他在手術室的第四天 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是這張桌子上的那個人 , 而是開心手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	97歲時 , 他每個月仍然進行二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	愛德華•拉林斯 , 103歲 , 一位活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末他喜歡在董事會上 , 丟掉羅斯特的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子就在這兒住在雙胞胎城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天都在舉重 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她走進她的根部 , 顏色是1994年的cadillseville , 穿著聖柏納多的高速公路 , 她仍然自願參加了七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我參加了19次硬幣探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是你唯一會見的人 , 穿越撒哈拉沙漠的腳踏車 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比馬吉•德頓更有傷害 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三個文化中有什麼共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的事是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地把它改成九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經做了兩次藍色的探險 , 和這些共同的決策者持有真實 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要解讀一系列的片段 , 沒有一個練習 , 至少我們認為練習的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之 , 他們建立了生命 , 讓它們不斷地被推動成為實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這一百歲的俄亥俄州的婦女正在上下 , 他們每天都坐在地板上 , 每天三十或四十次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店、教堂 , 或去朋友家 , 偶爾會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕要按鈕才能完成院子工作或房子 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒的卡路里和跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做刻意的實體活動時 , 他們很享受的事物 , 他們傾向走路 , 唯一證明方法能降低認知衰退 , 他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式建立生活 , 讓他們有正確的看法 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化需要時間下降 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的廣告家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans擁有這位祖先的神經
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你受傷或壓力時 , 會觸發一種叫做發炎反應的東西 , 這和阿茲海默症的所有事物有關 , 和心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天慢下來15分鐘 , 把炎熱狀態轉變成更加反炎狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有詞彙 , 以目的、ikigai , 像okinwans 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的目的 , 他們活在自己的人生中 , 值得七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天喝一點點酒 , 而不是對美國人來說很困難 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們通常會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	並不表示他們不會吃肉 , 但很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來避免過度濫用 , 讓它們在適當的時光下消失 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何聯繫 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先把家人放在家裡 , 照顧他們的孩子和老爸的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向信仰基礎的族群 , 值得四到十四年的預期壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的原因是他們屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們要麼出生就要麼積極地和對的人圍繞著自己 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從架構研究中得知 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友都肥胖了 , 有50%的機會會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 會隨時間產生可測量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	取而代之 , 如果你的朋友的想法是實體的活動、弓頭、腳踏車、園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝一點點 , 他們吃對了 , 他們很有信心 , 信任和值得信任 , 這會帶來巨大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不會成功 , 世界上歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動程序通常是一月開始 , 通常是十月份的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽時 , 在藥丸中沒有短期的固定條件 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想一想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能多花幾年的時間來增加生命 。 非常感謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	那種會導電的墨水 ; 一個從明顯的窗戶轉向開關的窗戶 ; 一個會製造音樂的水母 ; 所有的東西都存在 , 加拿大莫塔說:該是玩 。 馬塔會引導我們驚訝和酷的新材料 , 並建議我們能找出它們最好的方式去做實驗、粉紅色、有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用智慧材料玩耍 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父建造了一輛自行車和洗衣機 , 讓他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	那時我們知道東西是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何運作的 , 這樣我們才能建立並修復它們 , 或至少在有知情的決策中 , 決定要買什麼 。
