many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在二十世紀的第二半 , 許多這些做法都被遺失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者和開放原始碼模型把這些知識帶回我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層級 , 帶到下一個層級 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況 , 我們仍然知道像紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是什麼 , 以及它們是如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚訝的、具體的化合物 , 改變形狀的塑膠 , 會產生電力 , 顏料會改變顏色 , 會亮起來 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我來舉幾個例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電墨能讓我們不用傳統列印電路或電線來繪製電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	舉個例子 , 我們用它來創造觸覺感應器 , 藉由啟動這個小光來反應我的皮膚 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電墨水被藝術家使用 , 但近期的發展指出 , 我們很快就能用雷射印表機和筆 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張照片是用無色光傳導粒子注射的 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的加密器只會在邊緣散射光 , 在這整個表面上 , 當我打開燈時 , 它會發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	其中有兩個已知的應用程式包括內部設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱染色素會在特定的溫度下改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 設定在溫度上 , 只比環境更高 , 你可以看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的原理之一是 , 在嬰兒瓶中 , 嬰兒瓶中 , 它表示內容很酷 , 可以喝 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常被稱為智慧型材料的東西 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們將成為我們日常使用的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行車 , 科幻小說承諾我們 , 但是我們可以有圍牆 , 改變顏色的顏色 , 取決於溫度 , 轉動的鍵盤 , 轉動的窗戶 , 轉動的窗戶 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家 , 透過訓練 , 為什麼我今天要談智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物是如何運作的 , 也因為我相信我們應該更深入了解組成我們的世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的組合並不足夠 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難在很小的量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用在如何使用它們 , 很少有人說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以現在 , 它們主要存在於交易秘密和專利領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 修理男孩和我創建了一個專案 , 我們稱之為 「 開放材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是一個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 發表訊息 , 鼓勵其他人 , 隨何時都能貢獻 , 並將資源集合 , 如同我們自己研究的論文和教學 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型、集體產生的資訊庫 , 以智慧材料為基礎 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們要關心智慧材料如何運作 ? 它們是什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的事物 , 而我們不了解的 , 最後用的是塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們所使用的物品、衣服、房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有很大的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們生活在一個智慧材料的世界裡 , 我們應該知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的 , 創新總是被粉紅色者所燃燒 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	許多時候 , 業餘者 , 不是專家 , 一直都是來自山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩個科學家了解這一點 , 當他們在一個簡單的方法上發表一張文件 , 來做導電墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦bunker , 他完全沒有化學經驗 , 直到那時 , 閱讀這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間中複製這個實驗 , 只用自身的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至製作自己的vortex混合器 , 基於另一個科學家/maker的課題 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦發表了他的結果 , 包括他嘗試的所有事情 , 沒有用 , 其他人也能研究並繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的主要創新就是在芝加哥一間良好的實驗室裡 , 用廉價的材料和工具 , 創造出一個實驗 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這份工作 , 其他人可以在他左邊的位置 , 設想出更簡單的處理程序和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子 , 我想提一下她的項目的目的 , 是要強調材料的特質 , 同時專注於創造力和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備在他們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但在他們的設計中 , 限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是制定一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們免於準備好的限制 , 來教導我們這些材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的其中之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有銅帶 , 連接到mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoho研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 來自簡單銅膠帶 , 到導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造商漢娜出版了她的食譜讓任何人複製並複製它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙質電子學是最有希望的材料科學分支 , 它讓我們能夠創造更便宜且彈性的電子學 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的工藝作品 , 她分享她的發現 , 打開一連串的新可能性 , 這些可能性都是美感和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的是 , 我們用熱情和好奇心來創造 , 而我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常處理未經處理的問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現了其他的選擇 , 甚至更好的方法來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人用材料做實驗 , 越多的研究者願意分享他們的研究 , 製造出他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正為我們服務的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得tednelson應該有時候 , 在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你必須了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是大型的主體 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人在家裡設想 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 接受新興科技的先進知識 , 是確保我們對未來的說法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車進入玻璃泡 , 把門鎖住 , 壓住加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 雖然我們只能看到我們身後的少數車 。 但如果車子能和彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算每個人的最安全的路徑 ? 珍妮佛想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•療法:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能是可以避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車危險 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的其中一件事 , 但宗教的標誌和好運的標籤會出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛我們所知的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是16到19歲的人們死亡的主要原因 , 在美國 , 導致死亡和75%的意外 , 和毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是位在高速公路上的年輕司機 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙正在慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我站在煞車上 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這個傢伙不會慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停止了 , 死了 , 死了 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只需65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩在煞車上 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abs踢進去 , 車仍然不會停 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋部署 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道車子停下來了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 讓車子彼此交流 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想讓你們想想現在開車的體驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	關上車子 。 關上門 , 關上玻璃泡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你身在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導向一部分的路徑 , 在其他的金屬巨人中 , 以超人的速度來導航 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指引你兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你們所擁有的 , 眼睛不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但是人們要求你做這樣的事 , 你想要做一件事情 , 他們要做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路邊脫下來 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪裡 , 轉向 , 看看你的盲點 , 不用看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我要在這裡看還是在這裡看 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一份很棒的工作 , 選擇我們所關心的道路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過某樣東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺錯了或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數的意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 。 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得很清楚 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子彼此交換資料 , 我們不只能看到三輛車、三輛車 , 到右邊、左邊 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛 , 我們就能看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看到我們面前的車子的速度 , 看看那傢伙會走多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人下降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能覺得這不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 沒有汽車 , 不是不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在路上行走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在公開的路上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	很難預測未來的車子會在哪裡 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使當你在車子裡 , 一些摩托車手來了爆炸 ! 每小時85英哩 , 我知道你有這種經驗 , 沒有 「 走出哪裡 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在路上可能在過去的半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	十、二十、三十英哩後 , 有人看過那個人 , 一旦一輛車看到他 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他就位於地圖上 , 速度 , 估計他每小時要走85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為車子會知道 , 因為另一輛車會在他的耳朵上發聲 , 像是: 「 順便說一下 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 看著 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物品 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們是非常好的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達成目標 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 像是分享車子的位置資料 , 分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車裡有一台gps和一台攝影機 , 我很精確地知道我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子 , 有點像是 , 他們在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	另一輛車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有一個精確的點子 , 可以想像其他車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共享這些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	鮑勃教授和他的團隊做過電腦模擬當福茲估計結合時即使車子分享gps資料我們把這項研究從電腦模擬到機器人測試床上這些在機器人身上的感應器:stereo攝影機、gps以及2d雷射線 , 發現在系統中常見的雷射線 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還將短距離的無線電連接起來 , 機器人彼此交流 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此相聚時 , 它們會準確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們將越來越多的機器人加入混合中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	有一個問題 , 當你太多的聊天時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先順序 , 那就是預測模型能幫助你 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人汽車都在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你不會注意到這些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先優先考慮一個看起來有點偏離的傢伙
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他在走路 , 你知道他怎麼走 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道哪些司機需要警示要走出路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想怎麼讓每個人最好的警告 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	為什麼這些車子會說: 「 你需要走出路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它取決於兩件事:第一 , 車的能力 , 第二 , 司機的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道的 , 他們可能沒有在緊急情況下做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一系列的研究 , 做為駕駛狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測駕駛向前、向下看、向下看 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪些車子 , 最好的位置是去計算每個人的最安全路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些科技存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨最大的問題就是我們自願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常讓人困惑的概念 , 我們的車會看著我們 , 和其他車子談起 , 我們會在大西洋上往下走 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信這可以保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我不知道你在做什麼 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看一下你的牌號碼 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是件好事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請各位考慮一下 , 如果你真的不希望你背後的青少年分散的青少年 , 知道你很勇敢 , 你即將要停止 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的做法 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子對你說話 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路變得更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人peterdandis談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金 , 實現他的夢想 , 藉由一起進入大氣層 , 並在零g中體驗無重力的夢想 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短的談話、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdamandis在stephenhawkinterhroghrohwking的peterwk
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	那些認識我的人知道我有多熱情打開太空的面前 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給予世界專家重力體驗0重力時 , 這實在是不可思議的 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次在考古xprize上見到他 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們手持的競爭 , 第二個xprize , 第一個團隊在10天內完成100個人類基因組序列 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一種叫做基因組1000個人的基因組序列 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克雷格•凡特的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你到無重力之中 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	地球上唯一能體驗零的地方 , 其實是飛行傘 , 無重量的飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿一架飛機 , 飛越頂部 , 你有25秒的重量 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再往下看 , 你的重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你再做一次 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8 , 10分鐘的重量 , 美國太空總署訓練他們的太空人多久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬•霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一家政府機構和一家公司的飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你就要殺掉這個人了 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的允許 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在甘迺迪太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場新聞會議 , 我們宣佈了我們的意圖 , 讓他有25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果它成功了 , 我們可能會做三次拋物線 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼要去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他說 , 對我來說 , 非常感動 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命在不斷地冒著災難的風險 。
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果它不進入太空 , 人類就不會有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想要鼓勵大眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 帶到美國太空總署的飛機後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個捐款人 , 我們募集了一萬五萬美金給兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個伺服器 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液中 , 他的心跳率 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落的設施 , 在那裡 , 太空梭起飛 , 陸地 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的夥伴lichtenberg , 我小心地把他暫停成零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他到達那裡 , 請他去體驗無重力的感覺 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物線之後 , 你知道的 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他微笑了 , 我們說去了 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	實際上 , 我們在威斯安•牛頓大學的一個蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋有同樣的椅子 , 艾薩克•牛頓做了 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七個也是第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他很開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 正是我們的一生中 , 我們正朝著這個星球遷移 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這個史詩冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家大衛•波林斯基在細胞內演出3分鐘的刺激動畫 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky是一個細胞 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是個醫學插圖師 , 我來自一個稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大之後 , 我一直在看真相和美的表達 , 科學界的藝術和美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是很棒的一件事 , 它們都有很棒的一件事 , 會讓它們成為理想和美麗的事物 , 可以透過科學和數學來觀察 , 幾乎就像一個科學家想約會的理想混合雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真理的表達方式 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的東西 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 有時它們有時很有用 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以翻一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美 , 通常對不在科學領域的人來說是不對的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用一種方式形容美麗的事物 , 通常只能用你理解語言和語音 , 來表達真實和美的特質 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙的常數 , 有一個人類理想的理想 , 你可以看到生命必須從數字中演化出來 , 這些都是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	我從事醫學插圖師的訓練 , 自從我被教導 , 我父親是雕塑家和視覺導師 , 我想要找出一種方法來幫助人們理解真相和美 , 藉由使用動畫 , 來說明故事 , 告訴故事 , 讓人們不見得會被帶到的事物 , 可以被教導 , 並且可以被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生經常沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們所學到的是 , 擁有真實和美麗的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是比較的 , 重點是 , 事實和美的本質並不總是很明顯 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是雞湯的古老食譜 , 把雞煮成雞 , 直到味道消失了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我和哈佛大學的robertlue接到一通電話 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意改變哈佛的醫療和科學教育的做法 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始著手探索細胞的真與美 , 探索分子和細胞生物學中的真和美 , 讓學生能夠更大的了解這些事實 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可以把細胞的心智圖像當作大型、忙碌、大型複雜的城市 , 由微機械組成 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 來自世界各地的奈米技術專家 , 被自動導向、強大、精準、精準的裝置 , 由胺基酸所組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械的力量是細胞如何移動的 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	細胞如何複製 。 它們能發揮我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們賦予我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是想辦法把這個故事變成一種動畫 , 讓哈佛生物視野成為哈佛大學的中心 , 這個網站是哈佛分子和細胞生物學系的網站 , 除了所有文字的外 , 讓這些學生能夠輕易地把所有的東西放在一起 , 讓這些學生可以內化的視覺化視覺化的觀點 , 透過這個觀點來研究這個觀點 , 這樣他們就能真正地運用這些觀點 , 來了解他們的生命 , 以致於他們所擁有的熱情感 , 以此 , 讓他們能發揮自己的生命的熱情 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你有巨噬菌體 , 正在蒸發微細管 , 它們會觸摸微血管牆的表面 , 它們會從細菌牆上取得資訊 , 它們會得到外面的信息 , 在那裡 , 它們無法看見和感覺 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但這些資訊會讓它們停止 , 讓它們內化 , 需要製造出各種各樣的零件 , 來改變它們的形狀 , 試著脫離這個微鏡 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛科學家及資料庫模型合作 , 來確認它們是如何移動 , 找出它們是如何移動的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	找出方法 , 要怎麼做到這一點 , 實在是太實用了 , 但沒有那麼真實 , 細胞內的群眾會阻止病毒發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一部三分鐘的讀者最早製作的電影版本 。 這是我們製作的一個正在進行的專案計畫 , 接下來的四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看看這個 , 看到細胞製造這些步行機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為kineins , 採用相對大小的載荷 , 來挑戰一隻螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內部發電真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們彼此傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內的差異 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出果蠅需要的部位 , 來自原子核的資訊 , 可以讀取基因的分子 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 如果沒有這些小型的微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 這真的會在缺席這些機器的過程中 , 讓它變成現在的處境 , 克里斯 , 真的很危險 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是fedex送給細胞的人 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做松森 , 他拿了一堆全新的新製造蛋白質 , 到細胞中需要的位置 , 不論是為了一個細胞 , 不論是蛋白質 , 不論是為了製造東西或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人都有大約十萬個這些東西正在四處奔跑 , 現在 , 在你一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感受到多懶惰 , 你根本沒有做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你回家想想看 , 我希望你們能做的是想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到了細胞機械 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們了解了這一切 , 並相信我 , 我們就知道一旦我們知道發生了什麼事 , 我們將會有很大的控制權 , 能控制我們對未來世代所做的事 , 以及我們將會活得多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發現更多真相 , 和更多美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 非常令人驚訝 , 足以察覺到細胞需要它們的做法 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起工作 , 讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作 , 協助我們的身體 , 讓它們永遠看不到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝克•布蘭頓計畫要在她的車上住一年 , 見到這個國家 , 但當憂鬱和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的營地變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述她成為美國無家可歸的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、幸福、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、說故事、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:我是無家可歸的那一年 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個好奇的人 , 在22年內 , 我學會了很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事情就是變成看不見的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯工作 , 那是我父親去世的二月時 , 我決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡擊中了我 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我在做這件事的時候 , 有很多事要去感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 , 我決定住在一輛旅行車裡 , 要做這樣的事 , 就好像一個長的營地一樣 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我把我的貓、我的旋轉牛、我的營地 , 裝在1975年的雪梨車上 , 開車到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等同於一個永久的結構 , 甚至被壓縮 , 被視為一個人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到他人的負面認知能影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓它實現 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車子裡很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我常常在營地洗澡 。 我常常吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親的死亡就開始憤怒和憂鬱 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須得到全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個非常溫和的春天 , 變成一個非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	公園在任何地方都看不清楚我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 牠真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過一扇窗外 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗會去做小狗的日常照顧 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	無論何時 , 我都在辦公大樓裡使用員工洗澡 , 卡車停止 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者我在公共場所洗衣服 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度很少下降了華氏80度 , 使得睡眠很難或無法睡覺 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱氣中轉動 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	在我的冰層裡 , 幾小時內融化了 , 非常悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起去找公寓 , 或負擔不起的公寓 , 讓我可以有旋轉者和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄 , 所以我待在車子裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣使我生病到五十英尺外的公共廁所時 , 我晚上用桶和垃圾袋作為廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣進來時 , 溫度下降 , 停在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一系列的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每晚都在停車位 , 讓我避免被警察察覺 , 並被警察局限住 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感到失控了我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道發生了什麼事 , 但是我從有才華的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在車子裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商沒有掉下來 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天賦 , 我的誠實 , 我的價值觀 , 關於我的一切都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我轉向更深層的憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終 , 有人把我帶到無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣緊張、沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或很高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當許多無家可歸的人發現 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 你為什麼會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人不認為我是無家可歸的 , 但是我確實做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給了我憂鬱症的反應 。 我心想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆rusert , 一個全國知名的記者 , 在全國電視台上談到我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇關於我父親的文章 , 他死前的那一年 , 就在提姆的新書裡 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在做演說的電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到 , timrusert , 《會議》的前任者 , 談到我的寫作 , 當我住在華爾瑪的一輛車裡 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑是因為那時候我是作家還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 我找到了提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重返我的論文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我在和朋友一起衝浪時 , 生活在車子裡 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	接下來的一年夏天 , 我是一位職業記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在我的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再看不見 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬的人全職工作 , 都住在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會仍然汙名化、犯罪化 , 或在街道上生活 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸的無家可歸 , 主要還是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你碰到一個 , 加入他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	如果有希望的話 , 人類的精神可以克服任何事情 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡是無家可歸的海報 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們住在哪裡 , 他們睡在哪裡 , 或在任何時間的情況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一個沃爾瑪停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是能找到一種方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , thailand的《保險套》 , mechaiviravaida帶領我們走過這個國家的大膽計劃 , 從1970年代開始 , 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著很多的法蘭克 , 非常有趣 , 非常有效率地談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球性議題、健康、人口、科學、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviraida:保險套如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 有很多人生活在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定為此做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫或貧窮的減少方案開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭禁止計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 一系列的活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭計畫 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:去找孩子 , 去找媽媽 , 然後跟著家庭計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 也需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶你們回到我們需要這麼做的原因 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭的七個孩子都成長了3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥丸 。 」 我們有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把答案當作答案 , 我們沒有當作一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和助產士 , 同時也是婦女 , 在解釋如何使用藥丸時 , 做了很棒的工作 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	這真是太棒了 , 但卻佔了全國百分之二十 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人單獨做些什麼 , 然後說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了你看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 在黃色的標誌下 , 我希望他們還沒聽過 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂更大 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選擇的人就是我們選擇的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區裡都很知名 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很厲害 , 他們練習了他們的家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就在那裡 。 我們去找被視為問題的成因 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論在哪裡 , 都有人 , 都可以看船 , 賣東西 , 賣東西 , 賣香蕉、螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 只要你在泰國找到人 , 你會在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的 , 不是黃色的水 , 讓僧人在藥丸和保險套上灑水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片被送到全國 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	有些村莊的僧侶也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去了老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人去試著提供任何讓人類成為更好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去了老師們 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人教導家庭規劃一個新的字母a , 出生a , b , c , 保險套 , 我為iud , v做陰道檢查 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有一套蛇和梯子遊戲 , 丟掉 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何可行的計畫上登陸 , 你就開始前進 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像是: 「 媽媽每天晚上服藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 向前移動 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 。 搬到前面 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 。 再回來 , 再次開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣的 , 教育、課堂娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有相對的種族 , 我們有孩子的保險套冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久前 , 保險套被稱為女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會讓它變成保險套是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年引進了第一批小額貸款計畫 , 那些組織的女性說: 「 我們只想借錢給做家庭計劃的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上拿出一塊貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那就是他們所做的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年之後 , 它仍然持續著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 而是資助小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來管理它 , 由村民自己運作 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能幾乎看不到一個泰國男子 , 女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	然後我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助所有人 , 不管他們是否想要幫助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供陰道切除術 , 但特別是 , 美國人到隊友的前面 , 就在阿巴斯德的住宅中 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們這間酒店給了我們非常適合的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你一些午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 這一定是美國的煤炭 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你有兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	食物不是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我覺得熱狗會比較有象徵性 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這裡是這個 , 接著 , 名叫威利•波姆 , 他為美國援助工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他的陰道很熱 , 因為他的熱狗是一半的食物 , 他很高興 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國做了很多新聞 , 它也憤怒了一些人 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來 , 我會做很多事 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在這一切中 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟著我們 , 或者我們追蹤可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的案例 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強大的政府 , 我們沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病出現 , 撞到泰國 , 我們得要停止做許多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以 , 我們的工作並沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去參加軍隊 , 要求借300個電台 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們的槍比政府還多 , 他們的槍比政府還多 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們能否協助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數據之後 , 他們說: 「 沒錯 , 你可以使用所有的無線電站 , 電視台 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時我們到了飛機上 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	之後 , 我們得到了一個新的總理 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 你能來加入嗎 ? 」
he asked me in because he liked my wife a lot .	他問我是因為他很喜歡我的妻子 。
so i said , " okay . "	我說: 「 好吧 。 」
he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為國家愛滋病委員會的主席 , 增加了五十倍 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個部門、甚至法官 , 都必須參與愛滋病教育 , 我們說公共、機構、宗教機構 , 每個人都參與 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	這裡 , 每一位媒體人都必須接受愛滋病的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	我們給每個站了半分鐘額外的廣告 , 來賺更多錢 。
so they were happy with that .	所以他們很高興 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	接著 , 所有學校的愛滋病教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	這些是高中生教導高中生 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最好的老師是女孩 , 不是男孩 , 她們很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	這些女孩們圍繞著教導安全性愛滋病病毒 , 被稱為maatsa 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再走下一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三、四年級的小學 , 每個村莊的家庭 , 每個家庭都有愛滋病資訊 , 給每個家庭的保險套 , 給這些孩子 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有父母反對 , 因為我們試圖拯救生命 , 這是個救命 。
and we said , " everyone needs to be involved . "	我們說: 「 每個人都需要參與 。 」
so you have the companies also realizing that sick staff don't work , and dead customers don't buy .	所以 , 公司也意識到 , 生病員沒用 , 而死掉的客戶也不買 。
so they all trained .	所以他們都受過訓練 。
and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	然後我們拿著他的哈佛mba , 去學校和夜間 。
and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們很愛他 。 你需要一個符號 。
in every country , every program , you need a symbol , and this is probably the best thing he's ever done with his mba .	在每個國家 , 每一個程式 , 你都需要一個符號 , 這可能是他用mba所做的最好事 。
and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	接著 , 我們把保險套送到街上 , 到處都有 。
in taxis , you get condoms .	在稅收中 , 你得到保險套 。

and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧困中的人 , 取得信用信用必須是人權 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能像是朋友 , 但真正的朋友會在ted2013年給你微笑 。 在ted2013年 , kellerrinadodemomo , 一個能讓你在路上移動的聰明機器人 , 把一杯咖啡放在桌上 , 做出可程式的表情 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	克萊娜•里納多:一台小型機器人 , 由你的手機發電 。

not very many of you .	不是很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好吧 。 實際上 , 如果你不包括seba , 你們當中有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們在romotive上嘗試解決的問題 , 我和其他20位romotive的怪胎 , 對於解決這個問題很著迷 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以 , 我們真的想要建造一個任何人都能使用的機器人 , 不論你是八到八十個 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這真的是個很困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型可攜帶的機器人 , 不只能負擔得起 , 還必須是人們真的想要帶回家 , 帶著孩子回家 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人無法怪罪或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個你已經知道且愛你的iphone的機器人 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由控制iphone處理器的電力 , 我們就能創造出一個機器人 , 它可以使用wi-fi和電腦視覺 , 可用於150美元 , 這大約是過去這類機器人所需的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他是生物模式 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上是用攝影機在裝置上來追蹤我的臉 。

if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來這裡 , 他會轉過來跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會害怕其他生物 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以在很多方面 , romo就像一隻寵物 , 牠有自己的心智 。

so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是romo今天能做到的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的事物 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在谷歌開放框架上 , 叫做 「 街區 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖動並丟下這些連續程式碼的積木 , 創造出任何你想要的機器人的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫romo的行為 。

and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在真實生活中執行 , 執行程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有自豪的東西 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些wi-fi的機器人都互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們專注在建造能訓練的機器人上 , 是因為我們認為 , 個人機械人最有說服力的使用案件是個人的 。

so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為如果你在家裡有一個機器人 , 機器人應該是你自己的想像力 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道 , 不是十年或一千億美金 , 或大型的人類機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 像romo , 以及像你這樣的人的創造力 。
