author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和活躍主義者是阿拉伯女性、創造力、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 在這場演說中 , 熱情的定義 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•艾倫•艾倫說過熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 這真的很可怕 , 非常可怕 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡告訴各位一些熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有句猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼是真理 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 。 我想傳達的 , 遠勝於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我感興趣 , 有些故事直到我寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我知道我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫下巧合、預防、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我在2006年2月過世 , 直到我在義大利的奧林匹克旗下 ,
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為名人 。 現在人們意識到我在macy , 我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	容我告訴你我第四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克儀式的組織者之一 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗幟的一員 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這肯定是錯誤的身分 , 因為我可以從運動員身上得到的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在沒有步行者的體育場上行走 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是什麼笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有婦女會攜帶奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個婦女代表五大洲 , 三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然的 , 我會穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 一個制服 , 問了我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有一個視覺 , 在一個流暢的亂流中 , 看起來像是密西林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	二月中間 , 我發現自己在土耳其 , 那裡有熱情的群眾歡呼 , 那裡有80個奧運隊在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了所有東西在遊戲中競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得勝利 , 但運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一英吋的雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 除了訓練或運氣之外 , 重要的是心 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	全都是關於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅色海報覆蓋 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 , 不是總是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中的角色所需要的:一個充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks、異議者、異議者、外人、反叛者、問問題的人、彎曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座的各位一樣 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	一個有常識的人不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做好的配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了另一隻旗幟熊:三隻運動員 , 演員ssansarandon和蘇菲雅羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 有兩個充滿熱情的婦女:孟加利馬哈伊 , 肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主種植了三千萬棵樹 。 藉此 , 她改變了土壤 , 天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然還有許多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	媽媽媽 , 柬埔寨的活動家 , 熱情地對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 由男性強暴的小女孩 , 她們相信和非常年輕的處女有性關係 , 會治癒她們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	那些被迫收到五、十五個客戶的妓院 , 如果她們反抗 , 她們就會受到電力折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我收到了制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我一般穿的衣服 , 而是來自密西林人的服裝 , 我預期的不是很糟 , 真的很糟 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像是冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了蘇菲亞羅倫 , 所有美麗和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲亞超過七十歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很瘦、很高、很高 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有深水池 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視訪談中被問到: 「 她怎麼看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 , 我的背總是直立 , 我不會讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有一些自由建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有嚇人 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有竊聽 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有養育 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有說這句話 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 大聲聲聲播放者宣佈奧運國旗 , 音樂從這裡開始 , 同樣的音樂從這裡開始 , 愛滋達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲亞羅倫站在我面前 , 她比我還高 , 不要算頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她走得很優雅 , 像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 把旗子放在肩膀上 。 我在我的指尖上伸出旗子 , 這樣我的頭其實就在該國旗下了 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的相機都在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現在蘇菲亞的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	大部分男人都喜歡去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘都是奧林匹克體育館裡的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我說這句話時 , 我的丈夫被冒犯了 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們在私下的做法通常要花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不該私下採取 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有四分鐘的記載 , 因為我不想忘記 , 年齡破壞了我的大腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠地帶著奧運會的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這是個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 在剛果的特魯西難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和離失所的人都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以在剛果死亡營中稱這個地方 , 因為那些沒有被殺害的人 , 會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕的女人 , 蘿絲.地圖 , 和她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她是懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她去看她的丈夫被折磨和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她還能讓她活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子切斷腫瘤 , 將它和牠自己的頭髮結合 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把雙胞胎命名為營地的指揮者 , 給予黑人茶 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當軍人在她的牢房中強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她抓住她 , 拒絕放下去 , 即使他們拿著槍頭向她 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了16個月 , 接著 , 幸運地 , 美國年輕人的熱情心 , 薩哈•查諾夫 , 她把她送進美國救援飛機 , 羅斯•地圖 , 和她的九個孩子最後到達鳳凰城 , 在那裡 , 他們活著和茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里 , 地圖是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書裡的主角是強壯且充滿熱情的女性 , 例如羅塞•地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不會把它們放上去 , 也不需要這樣 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都和女性合作 。
i know them well .	我很熟悉他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古代 , 在世界末期 , 在父權天主教和保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪在我五歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者雖然這個詞還沒到智利 , 所以沒有人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 有很高的代價來支付我的自由 , 並且質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能支付它 , 因為每次我收到的炸彈 , 我就能發出兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒在她的二十歲時 , 她告訴我女權主義是約會 , 我應該繼續 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場難忘的戰鬥 , 女權主義是約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒和所有人一樣的特權女性來說 , 現今世上大部分的姊妹仍然被強迫去做早婚、妓女、強迫勞工 , 她們有她們不想要或不能餵飽的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法控制自己的身體或生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被毆打、有時被殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	至今大部分的西方女性被稱為女性主義是侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有性感 , 但讓我向你保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我發炎 , 我也因為缺乏男性而遭受嚴重的痛苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義沒有死 , 毫無意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 改變它 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為噬菌體、金星、或任何你想要的東西 ; 名字並不重要 , 只要我們了解它的意義 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的例子 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉村莊的小婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	今年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫衛生學家 , 她在三週的假期中擔任志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好要清潔牙齒 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生、沒有牙醫 , 診所只是充滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一排女人等了好幾個小時才被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人在痛苦的痛苦中是因為她有幾隻腐爛的腫瘤 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道 , 唯一的解決方案就是拉出壞牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒著很多險 , 且她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶了一些新藥 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢和熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她是一位禱告師 , 然後她繼續做手術 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 鬆開的病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生學家拉出更多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次回到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一位病人和丈夫在等她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來就像是水手 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、憤怒、威脅要殺掉美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但後來翻譯解釋病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打敗她 , 因為她不在家裡準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬名女性生活在這裡 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然美國婦女有三分之二的勞動力 , 但世界上的資產少於百分之一 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於同一工作 , 如果他們薪水很低 , 他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟的獨立性 , 且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制收入的能力、繼承和有利於社會 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村落 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女性談話 , 解釋土地是荒蕪的 , 因為她們有砍伐和賣樹 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們去種新的樹和水 , 一滴下來 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在大約五到六年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤很豐富 , 而村莊則被拯救 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最後退的社會總是把女人放下 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這種顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善事業忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊錢給女性的專案 , 每一塊20塊美金給男性的專案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	讓它們能改變一切 , 比科技、設計和娛樂更重要 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性合作 , 結合、有知情和教育 , 能帶來和平和繁榮 , 帶給這個明星 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民的 , 主要是女人和小孩 , 他們是相對的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們所擁有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人都在問的問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有世界秩序是有道理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 生活的品質和生活的品質 , 不僅是給所有人的特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月 , 我看到一幅展覽fernandobotero的畫作在加州柏克萊圖書館 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了帶著波特羅作品的紐約畫廊之外 , 已經敢於展示這幅畫 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的大畫作 , 包括伏特兒的風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把這些影像從我腦中得到 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是 「 無名 」 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 迫使其他的包裝接受現實並遵循規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則不斷地改變 , 但它們總是有益 , 而在這個例子中 , 被欺騙的效應 , 這種效應在經濟上並不完美 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待的技巧從梯子的頂部移到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和小孩 , 特別是窮人 , 都在底部 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最親密的男人 , 也有人可以虐待女人或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我是用較少的性別、收入、種族、階級來餵飽的權力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我想 , 該是我們文明的根本改變的時候了 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對於真正的改變 , 我們需要女性能量在世界的管理中 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要很多女性在權力的位置 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是年輕的心智 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老年人是無希望的 ; 我們必須等待他們死 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很樂意有蘇菲雅羅倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但根據一個選擇 , 我寧願有天使的熱心 , 瑪麗 , 瑪麗 , 瑪麗 , 珍妮和玫瑰地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變得好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要讓它變得更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 它是可能的 。 看看這房間裡的所有知識、能量、才華 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們離開我們的迷戀 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐是被服務的 。 但 , 所有的食物都來自哪裡 ? 建築師卡林•史黛爾討論要餵飽城市的每日奇蹟 , 並展現古老的糧食路線如何塑造現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡莉琳史黛爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最棒的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們把它視為理所當然 , 如果我們進入商店或餐廳 , 或是進入這個劇院的foer , 大約一個小時 , 會有食物等著我們 , 神奇地來自某處 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到 , 倫敦的每一天城市大小 , 足夠的食物必須被生產、運輸、購買、吃、丟棄、丟棄 , 和地球上的每一天都一樣 , 都市是非常了不起的 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的事物 , 忘了 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃 , 其實我們和古老的祖先一樣依賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們進入城市 , 越來越多的自然世界被轉化成非凡的景觀 , 像我身後的那個景觀 , 它在巴西的馬托格羅索 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但少數人見到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多這些地景也不只餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們搬到城市裡 , 越來越多人吃肉 , 所以每年全球有三分之一的穀物被餵食給動物 , 而不是給我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	既然它需要三倍的穀物 , 實際上是十倍的穀物來餵飽人類 , 如果它通過動物的第一條 , 那就不是非常有效率的餵養我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個更嚴重的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 估計我們所居住在城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	也有人估計會有兩倍的肉和乳的消耗 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	肉類和都市主義正在舉手 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會帶來巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 60億隻飢餓的肉食 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們繼續這樣下去 , 這是我們無法解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九百萬公頃的雨林損失 , 創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時 , 我們也失去了相當於現存的可耕種 , 以鹽化和肥料 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	每一卡路里需要10卡路里才能生產出每一卡路里的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有很大的成本生產食物 , 我們其實不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前有一半的食物會被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在長期的過程中 , 我們甚至沒有妥善管理這個星球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人肥胖 , 同時又有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒什麼意義 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為80%的全球貿易現在被五家多國企業控制時 , 它是很嚴格的照片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們進入城市 , 世界也在擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是一個無法永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們是怎麼來到這裡的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答這個問題稍微容易一點 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程在古老的東邊 , 被稱為肥沃清潔 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 正如你所見 , 它的形狀很明顯 。
and it was also fertile .	同時也是肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 這裡有兩個非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 大約是在同一個地方 , 同時發生的 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並不意外 , 因為農業和城市是互相連結的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為它被我們古老的祖先所發現 , 首次產生出足夠的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久的居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處是什麼樣子 , 我們會看到它們是完整的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被農地包圍 , 由大型寺廟複雜的土地包圍 , 如同在ur的大型寺廟複合 , 實際上 , 正是精神化 , 主要的食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是組織收成的神廟 , 將收成物聚集在穀物中 , 提供給神 , 接著 , 神沒有吃回人的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的精神和生理生活都是由穀物主宰 , 維持它們的收穫 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	羅馬在第一世紀時有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市如何自給自足 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我所謂的 「 古代食物旅程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以接觸海 , 這使得它可以從很長一段路外進入港口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界中唯一能做到的辦法 , 因為在道路上 , 運送食物是非常困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	很明顯地 , 食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地打擊像卡瑟和埃及的戰爭 , 只為了讓他們的穀物保存下來 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說帝國的擴張真的很長 , 把軍事化的購物速度拿出來 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上我很愛這個事實 , 我只需要提到:羅馬以前從倫敦到牡蠣 。 我覺得這很不尋常 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過胃口來塑造它的蜂巢 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事情也發生在工業時代 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看17世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它是從thames的底部 , 沿著這張地圖 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場到城市的南邊 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	這條道路從他們走到廉價的路 , 也是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看這些街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道在300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 對魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是靠河流來的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 據名的說法是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代中期一直在營運 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真是太不可思議了 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	所有其他人都在帶著手機 , 看起來像是磚塊 , 有點像在港口上販賣的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	城市裡的食物是另一回事:一旦它的根在城市中被建立起來 , 它們很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是很不一樣的故事 , 因為動物當然可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的肉類大多來自西北 , 蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來到最北邊的城市 , 這就是為什麼smithfield , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 位在那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	詩人來自東方的角落 , 諸如此類的 , 到東北 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像是氣象女人在做這件事 。 不管怎樣 , 鳥類都用小畫布保護著 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當他們抵達便宜的東部時 , 他們就賣掉了 , 這就是為什麼它叫作 " 波音 " 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任何城市在工業時代之前建造的地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物來到它 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你實際上可以看到它是如何由食物形成的 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名字 , 這給了你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在一個星期五的生活中 , 你在星期五去買你的魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它充滿食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一購買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年的史密斯菲爾德的照片 , 你可以看到 , 在這樣的城市中 , 很難想像你的食物來自哪裡 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐 , 可能是三天前在窗外凝結 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機的城市 , 也是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年偉大西方的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物就不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被困在視覺和心中 , 被屠殺 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們被鐵軌進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 要開始發展城市 , 任何大小和形狀 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前 , 城市被地理限制了 ; 以前 , 他們得要用非常困難的實體方式來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們的確是從地理學中解放出來的 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	正如你從倫敦的地圖上看到的 , 在火車出現的90年後 , 火車出現了 , 很容易被動物送到腳下 , 到大型的水泥 , 非常難供應任何人腳下的動物或人類 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了之後 , 真的是這個過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最後的解放 , 完全和大自然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市缺乏氣味、缺乏混亂 , 絕對沒有人夢想過這片土地 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們所得到的食物是他們在他們的車子裡開車到戶外的一個箱子 , 一個禮拜的購物中心回來 , 想知道在地球上該怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的是我們與食物和城市之間的關係 , 都完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡 , 我們有過去是中心 , 城市的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它以前是社交活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 現在我們加入水 , 或一些蛋 , 如果你製造蛋糕或某種東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是在包裝上讀到一張標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不重視食物 , 也不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不要信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評估它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的一個很諷刺的是 , 他們承諾要讓它變得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由使它可以在任何地方建造城市 , 任何地方都可以 , 它們真的能讓我們和最重要的關係連結 , 也就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	同時 , 它們也讓我們依賴系統 , 只有它們才能實現 , 如我們所見 , 無法永續發展 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 湯瑪斯自問了什麼 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他書《烏托邦》的頭條 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列半獨立的城市如果聽起來很熟悉 , 每一天 , 每個人基本上都是養殖場 , 在他們的後園裡種植蔬菜 , 然後一起吃餐 , 諸如此類 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為你可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本訂購原則 , 儘管它從來沒有這麼想過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 遠景 , 伊本霍華 , 《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的點子:一系列半獨立的城市 , 小小的都市 , 有可耕地 , 加入了鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的順序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但和霍華的視覺無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	而這些烏托邦的想法 , 就是它們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾所使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為希臘的雙倍發揮 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它也可能意味著一個好的地方 , 或沒有任何地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 , 一個想像性的事物 。 我們無法擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念化的工具 , 來思考人類的深層問題 , 讓它無法使用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 來自古希臘的 「 西托 」 、 「 食物 」 、 「 接觸 」 的地方 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以用食物作為一個強大的工具 , 一個概念的工具 , 設計工具 , 來改變世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 西托邦會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我想它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是狗的臉 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生活中心的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被慶祝、被享受 , 人們花時間去做 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這就是我們社會中的食物應該在哪裡 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非你有像這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便說一下 , 這些人也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到前面的食物 , 想想看 , 可以盯著一堆原始蔬菜 , 並且認出它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為沒有這樣的人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地方了 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這點 , 因為這是男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路 , 食物在當地種植的市場 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是城市的社會生活 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有這些 , 你就不能有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 不僅僅是一片零和的商品 , 在某些不見的地獄裡 。
cows with a view .	牛有視野 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽謙遜 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的社區專案 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一個溫室 , 在那裡 , 孩子們會告訴所有食物 , 種植自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有個叫kevin的植物 , 或者是屬於一個叫kevin的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這些企劃試圖與大自然重新連結的項目是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 坐在烏托邦 , 對我來說 , 是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 它意識到 , 西托邦已經存在於各處的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是加入它們 , 把食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就會停止將城市視為是大型、大都市、不生產性的爆炸 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 不可避免地連接在一起 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這不是一個偉大的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再生產這樣的食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要考慮更多的永續生態 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張圖片總結了我認為我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	它是一種重新思考食物如何塑造我們的生活方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂的《好政府》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧國家 , 國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要我們問阿布羅吉歐•洛倫澤蒂 , 如果他今天畫了這張照片 , 他會怎麼樣 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天的好政府會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個急迫的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	我們必須問 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的東西 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解 , 世界也是我們吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為一個非常強大的工具 , 來塑造世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	在21世紀 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯看到了宗教的角色:它的教條會否分裂我們 ? 或者它會讓我們團結起來 ? 她會評估全世界的信仰 , 重新審視黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted , 全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal-2009年 , 暴力 , 暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	卡倫•阿姆斯壯:讓我們重現黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我意識到同情心的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出他們自己的版本 , 稱為黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 會出現在正面的版本中 , 「 總是對待他人 , 就像你想要對待自己一樣 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本: 「 不要對其他人做你不想做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現會讓你疼痛 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去衝突任何其他人的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 也因為它成功 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們執行黃金法則時 , 他們說: 「 整天、每一天 , 」 不僅僅是做好好好事 , 再回到貪婪和自我主義的生活 , 而是每天 , 把自己從世界的中心 , 放到另一邊 , 超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你進入了 「 神 」 、nirvana、rama、tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超出我們所知的 , 超出我們所知的 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道這一點 , 宗教生活的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有幾個奇妙的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 他們爭論abstrustrines , 或說是仇恨的協議 , 或對同性戀或其他類似的東西 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到我在和宗教人士談話時 , 會看到一種完全相互的表情 , 因為人們通常想要對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我很感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地帶我上書 , 把我帶到21世紀 , 讓我能和一個比我想像中更廣泛的觀眾說話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	若我們無法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們才能對待所有人 , 不論他們是誰 , 儘管他們跟我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們將會有一個可行的世界來對抗下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性的社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以一起生活在和平 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 卻被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 這不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種同理心的想像力 , 把你自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有一個選擇 , 似乎對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們要不是要把信仰帶到外面 , 強調信仰的信仰 , 或我們可以回到拉比 , 拉比希爾 , 耶穌的年長的現代教義 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 請他總結整個猶太教義時 , 說: 「 這對你是有害的 , 不要對你的鄰居做 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉 , 所有其他的都只是留言 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	瑞比和早期教會的父親說 , 任何被破壞的文字符號 , 都不合法 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要復原這些精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只會發生 , 因為愛情的靈魂下降 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須實現這一點 , 我們可以利用ted所介紹的現代溝通 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經非常熱衷於所有伴侶的反應 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群團體會用這張圖來治癒分裂 , 最近在新加坡社會中出現 , 一些國會成員想要在政治上實現它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一項藝術展 , 領導藝術家將要帶領人們、年輕人 , 並告訴他們 , 同情也是所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區正在舉辦活動和討論 , 討論關於同情心的核心 , 以及所有信仰 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那裡 , 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教導 , 這就是我們錯了的地方 , 唯一集中在相信abstrustrustrines 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算要做這次死亡的日子 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續與我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 教育和刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們失去同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常認為這只是對某人感到抱歉的意思 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但如果你想一想 , 你就不會了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 協助解決我們對其他人有的刻板印象 , 把我們從另一個人身上分離出來 。
the same applies to educators .	相同的教育家也是如此 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到動態、動態和挑戰同情的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時 , 它也要求有敏銳的智能 , 不僅僅是美味的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 去探索他們和他人的傳統中同情的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵大家對不停的說話的敏感度 , 如此一來 , 是因為人們有這個主題 , 或缺乏他們的信仰 , 他們覺得有能力去挑戰不停的言論 , 不論他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖、來自產業的資本 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把圖表放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在舊的世界裡 , 一群人坐在一間房間裡 , 還在發聲 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹一個全新的思維和展示想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為那就是ted的好奇心 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專長如果我們一起加入 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有些時候 , 問題似乎很不可思議 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想要引用一句話 , 最後的句子是英國作者 , 牛津作家 , 我不常引用c.lewis說的話 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一篇讓我印象深刻的文章 , 自從我還是學童時 , 我就讀到了 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	這本書在《四個愛》中 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他分辨出愛情 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字時 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	然後他比較友誼 , 當兩個人站在一邊時 , 肩膀肩膀肩膀 , 雙眼固定在共同目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要彼此相愛 , 但我們也能成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我很確信 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我覺得在vevey的小小決心中 , 很強烈地感受到 , 當所有不同說服的人聚在一起 , 一起工作 , 一邊工作 , 一邊工作 , 一邊是為了共同的目標 , 差異融化 。

he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後漸漸地在建築的頂部工作 , 由公寓檢查每個電視台 , 檢查每個連結 , 希望找出問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他向上爬 , 終於是大樓 , 接著是小樓梯 , 直到他抵達大樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開了閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 還有一張桌布圍繞著建築的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題解決了 , 包拉索的所有人都很快樂 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決他自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在所要做的 , 就是用一個完美的桌子 , 等著她到來 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但看來不夠多 , 足以傳達我對羅馬的意見 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 嗯 , 我會做個偏執 , 我會進去 , 下面我會展示這些東西的成長 , 並且顯示它們的形狀 , 以此類推 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最愛的片段和片段放到萬神廟裡 , 讓它們保持尺度 , 讓你們可以看到聖誕節的頂部和金字塔 , 以及布拉曼特的側面 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這張圖是我認為 , 也許是piranesi去見escher的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到 , 我開始失去控制權 , 也失去了希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	這裡有一條非常薄的藍線 , 可以穿過這條路 , 將它包含在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不只是收集和儲存資訊的好處 , 它是一系列層 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層剝去另一層 , 我們把它們視為頁面 , 做某種特定的方式 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們想成是層層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是層層層層層層 , 垂直層層次 , 我想 , 只要我把頁面剝開 , 讓我可以用正確的方式來表達層層層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部份建築的黏土覆蓋了傷疤 , 數世紀以來 , 這些結構已經被適應 , 而不是被拆除 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做摺疊頁 , 讓你張開它 , 看看它背後的意思 , 我所謂的疤組織 。

you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭部的頁面包裹在那短暫的時段 。

and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我用另一種方式把這本書轉過來 , 我們就在萬神廟的前面 。

" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 讓我陷入困境 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果那是一顆熱鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 家園的奧德賽 」 。

it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	它是教堂頂部的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天就離開了 , 做正常的鴿子 。 回來 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網絡覆蓋 , 這樣鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以它現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另一個地方生存 , 這使我能穿過我最愛的東西 , 我們從最高的地方開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回顧家人的生活 , 這不一定是件好事 , 但它確實能把鴿子帶回來 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該用某種方式參與其中 。

and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬上屋頂 , 所有的鴿子 , 紅色的氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:只要他失去一隻鴿子 , 他就會把鴿子帶到城市的牆上 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古老的羅馬客服中 , 死者從未埋在牆上 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是個很可怕的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這將會是很長的一段路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了一次 , 如果包裝不行 , 如果故事不在任何地方 , 我就想出了標題 , 希望一個標題會把我踢到正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它會專注在我身上 , 我甚至會做標題 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題的頁面 , 最終促使我進入我安定的解決方案 , 一個年輕女子的故事 , 她在羅馬城的牆外傳遞一則訊息 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子在這上面飛下來 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓、松鼠等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你就會看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 它就變得很必要 , 試著傳達它的感覺 , 不要真的移動它 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	在克塞蒂斯的金字塔上 , 這些對你來說似乎很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 ,
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件最多謀殺的鴿子不做的事:它需要一趟風景的路徑 , 這是我覺得要把這本書延伸到四頁之外的裝置 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞著哥倫坡繞過聖母院的教堂 , 繞過了宇宙的聖母院 , 以及海克力士的寺廟 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和palazofrazofranesssssse設計的石頭是來自哥倫坡的狹窄逃跑 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們在campodefiri上掉下來 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這完全是認同任何規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的規則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出這裡的消失點在火星上 , 和其他幾個在克里蒙亞 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖塔馬里亞•德拉•德拉的前面 , 在那裡 , 足球賽正在進行 , 我們被足球打擊 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是一個非常糟糕的圖像 , 被足球撞擊 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的碎片:還有聖母峰 , 有一顆足球 , 有一隻鳥 , 一隻鳥 , 沒有發生 , 所以我得要重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想要看到聖誕老人貝拉的速度 , 這些書非常靈活 , 非常互動 , 只是把它轉過來 , 用另一種方式看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過聯盟 , 我們可以看到影響是紅線捕捉到的 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類會把自己拉到中世紀大樓中 , 只有少數的中世紀大樓 , 靠近聖塔格尼斯教堂 , 繞著圓頂向下看 , 我們已經提到 , 看到並飛過了幾次 ; 那裡有四個河流 , 然後超越了美妙的bormini聖城區 , 阻止了266英呎長的神石 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡面轉動 , 因為我們正在飛行 , 我們不用在這個特殊的時刻擔心重力 , 所以這張圖可以在頁面上隨意調整 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會變得有點興奮 , 這並不讓人意外地模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過我剛提到的美妙的牆 , 充滿了我所談到的混合物 ; 美麗的雕刻設在牆上 , 上方的 「 律師 」 標誌 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們抵達palazo的庭院 , 那是我們的目的 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一個小窗戶 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把訊息從鳥的腿中移除 , 這是牠說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看畫板時 , 我們看到他正在努力的其實是鴿子所拍攝的地圖 , 紅線穿過所有視覺 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 我們就完成了這種理解的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些範例 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究者skylarbbit在自組裝上工作 , 而不是建立某樣東西 , 我們可以創造出一些材料 , 大量的dnazips本身 。 這是個很大的概念 。 tibbit讓我們看到三個自組裝的項目 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbit:我們能否做出製造自己的東西 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想給你們看我們製造東西的方式 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信很快我們的建築和機器會自我組合、複製和修復 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要給你們看我相信的是目前的製造狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在目前的製造狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、新、令人興奮的新科技 , 鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年的組裝時間 , 兩百五十萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒內摺疊 , 或者有三十億鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜度 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠比我們所能建造的任何東西 , 遠比任何能建造的複雜得多 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們比能源更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以為自己修復壽命 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 天體系統有個超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將之轉化為我們的建築環境 , 那就有一些令人振奮的潛力來建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為那就是自我組裝的關鍵 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中自行組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 來讓我們的建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們建築物如何運作的dna
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的零件 , 可以用那段序列來摺疊 , 或重組 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能激發的能量讓我們的部位能夠從計畫中折疊起來
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要一些錯誤的修正方法 , 來確保我們成功地建立我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	我要給你們看一些計畫 , 是我的同事和我在麻省理工學院努力達成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	首先是麥克羅和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些計畫是大規模的可重組的機器人 , 8英尺 , 12英尺長 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們嵌入了機械電裝置 , 感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你將你想要的東西摺疊成一系列的角度 , 負120、0、0、0、120、負120、負120 , 類似的東西 。 所以一系列的角度 , 或轉動 , 然後通過弦來將這個序列寄出 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都把訊息傳遞給負面的120 , 它會轉移到那裡 , 然後傳遞給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些都是聰明的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 他們在這個專案上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的能帶來光明:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 成千上萬美金 , 許多人小時都做了這個八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人嵌入每一部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看被動的大自然 , 或是被動地嘗試重新設計程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它又更進一步 , 它嘗試有實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了計算的最基本的元件 , 數位邏輯閘門 , 直接進入你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nandgates 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一台超載體 , 即將完成你的運算 , 而你有兩個輸入的電子 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是用戶的輸入 , 當你在打破你的磚塊 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前面的磚塊裡出來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會給你一個3d空間中的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要的磚塊中加入 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它會計算它之前所做的事 , 以及你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三度空間中移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , [1]輸入等同等於0的輸出 , 下降了 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	右手邊的是0 , 0 , 輸入是1輸出 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的東西的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	他們把所有資訊都嵌入其中 , 包含在建構的內容中 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱之為自我複製 , 因為你的結構包含了特定的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入來告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有一些東西可以爬上去 , 讀取它 , 並且可以在一個地方輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有外部指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個專案叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是我們目前最令人興奮的自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要重組性和程式性 , 讓它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們偏頗了 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	每一個鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要轉右轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	當你組裝鏈 , 基本上是程式設計 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你告訴每個單位是否應該轉向右邊或左邊 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖鏈時 , 它就會折疊成你編寫的任何組合 , 像這樣的 , 一個螺旋 , 或者 , 在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體彼此相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以編寫任何三維形狀或三維立體的形狀 , 完全被動化成這個鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來的意義是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們 , 自我組裝的新可能性、複製、修復我們的物理結構、建築、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那之後 , 你就有電腦運算的新可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚頭都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是很驚人的平行和分配的運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這很令人振奮 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我剛剛展示的這些項目 , 只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們能實現這些新的自我組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過海洋深處的兩次深處 。 下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和探險家nathanwolfe提出這個答案:幾乎所有的一切 。 我們都可以開始 , 他說 , 帶著不可思議的世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾夫:要探索什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我造訪了威斯康辛 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一個偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然史博物館的期間 , 安德魯帶領一系列的探險 , 來到特殊的區域 , 就像在戈比沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來他說 , 印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特時 , 我給了一群中學學生公開的演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡要告訴各位 , 如果ted的演講比ted還要嚇人的話 , 它會試著保持一千個12歲的一群人的注意力 , 給45分鐘的演講 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	演講結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 我真的很困惑 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 很多人認為地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 下一代他們必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到一個重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	到底有沒有什麼意義讓我們探索地球的存在嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	它讓我回想起我最喜歡的生物學探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一位未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁•貝納克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草流行疾病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他把感染的果汁從菸草植物中除去 , 他會透過更小的濾嘴過濾出來 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了他認為一定有比當時所知的細菌還小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個名字給他的神秘代理人 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在發現病毒時 , beijerinck打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒佔據了地球上大部分的基因信息 , 比其他生命形式的遺傳信息還要多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 對於這個世界的實際應用 , 像是天花消滅疫苗 , 一種疫苗對抗子宮頸癌 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類乳腺病毒造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , 尼傑克發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道地球上大部分的基因信息的形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些令人驚訝的工具讓我們探索未知的世界 , 例如深度測序 , 使我們能做得更多 , 不僅僅是滑雪地表 , 去觀察特定物種的個別基因組 , 而是去觀察整個陳述微生物群落 , 在我們身邊 , 去記錄這些物種中的所有基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技術應用到土壤到皮膚中的東西 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們正常做這個實驗 , 來找出疫情的成因 , 正是造成疫情的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓你們了解這如何運作 , 想像一下我們從你們每一個人身上拿了一把捲餅 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們常常會尋找呼吸性病毒 , 例如流感 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們首先會看到的是非常大量的遺傳信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究遺傳信息 , 我們會看到很多常見的疑問 , 當然 , 人類的基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大多來自鼻子中完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了一件非常令人驚訝的事 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始檢視這些資訊時 , 我們會發現在你的鼻子裡 , 大約百分之二十的基因信息並不符合任何我們從未見過的植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們研究這種資料的小群體 , 我們當中有幾個人開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們之前看到的任何東西 ; 它和我們遺傳信息中的未知大陸一樣 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有百分之二十的基因信息是許多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對穩定的血液中 , 大約百分之一到兩分之二的信息是暗物質無法被分類 , 也不能被我們之前看過的東西配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人造的 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度測序工具相對是新的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得越來越精確 , 我們決心這些資訊是一種生命形式 , 至少有些是生命形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 只是在他們的嬰兒身上 , 有非常令人興奮的可能性:生命中埋藏在這種基因信息中 , 未被發現生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探究a、t、c、g , 我們可能發現一個全新的生命類型 , 像是beijerinck , 會徹底改變我們對生物學的本質 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許可以讓我們辨識出一種癌症的原因 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或是在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣佈 , 和史丹佛、加州理工學院及加州大學和加州大學的同事合作 , 我們正在開展探索生物暗物質 , 來探索生命的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 形成我們地球上大部分的遺傳信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆我們可能完全沒有意識到新的生命階級在我們的鼻子之下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	真的 , 我們可能已經掌握了地球上的所有大陸 , 我們可能發現了所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不代表地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的一課 , 例如來自威斯康辛州的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為 , 如果我們說這堂課 , 像這樣:不要假設我們目前認為的全面故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在任何你選擇探索的領域之後 , 去探索黑暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊有未知的未知 , 他們正等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇的科學家daviddeutsch把理論物理放在後部討論一個更急迫的問題:我們物種的生存 。 第一步是解決全球暖化 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛deutsch在我們宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以 , 我會試著這麼做 , 但我想要從大家已經知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 是歷史上大部分的記錄 。
