and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是 , 地球、太陽系、環境 , 或其它東西 , 獨一無二的適合維持我們的演化或創作 , 如同過去所想 , 我們的存在 , 最重要的 , 我們的未來生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可思議的 , 而宇宙是不可思議的 , 我們只仰賴太空船 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家已經知道的是 , 與大部分人類歷史的信仰相反 , 人類不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金所說的 , 我們只是典型的星球表面 , 繞著典型的恆星繞著一般的星球 , 繞著典型的星系 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道的兩件事就是說我們在一個非常不尋常的地方 , 獨一無二的安排等等 , 第二個則是說我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其當你把這兩種深層的真理看待 , 以便你的生活決策 , 就會變得有點衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個例子開始 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 咱們來看看四周 , 看看隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學圓柱 , 完全不典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要在同一個方向走幾百英哩 , 再回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆壁或化學氣質 , 你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你走得遠 , 你就會看到太陽、太陽系、恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為恆星在星系中 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 在宇宙中 , 沒有任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再進一步 , 直到我們在銀河之外 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 在我們面前 , 有巨大的星系 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此時 , 我們已經有十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍在宇宙中一個典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到典型的地方 , 你必須走一千倍 , 才能進入國際間的空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	在巨大的費用上 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 讓外加空間的觀點 , 呈現出來自星際空間的觀點 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能否把燈關掉 , 請看 , 我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美的你在星際間的太空中 , 完全是黑暗的 , 黑暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	黑暗 , 如果你看最近的星星 , 那顆星會像超新星爆炸 , 而你正直接盯著它看 , 當它照射到你時 , 你仍然無法看見一個星星 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙是如此的巨大和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星太亮了 , 所以很棒的一件事 , 超新星會在數光年之內殺死你 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 來自星際空間 , 到目前為止 , 你甚至看不到 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	在絕對零度上 , 它也很冷 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它非常空白 。 真空的密度比目前地球上最高的真空低一百萬倍 。 正是典型的地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	而這正是這個地方的典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	請把燈光放回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在 , 我們要如何知道遙遠的環境 , 如此不一樣 , 外星人 , 從我們所習慣的任何地方來 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球是我們的環境 , 我們的形式就是創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	那意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 遠遠超過我們剛剛的意思 , 用望遠鏡 , 然後你會看到類似星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 quasars 」 。 quasars原本是指量子極物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像星星 , 但它們不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道幾十億年前 , 距離數十億光年 , 銀河系中心的物質瓦解了超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場會引導引力崩塌的能量 。 有些物質 , 以巨大的噴射機的形式 , 以我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理學幾乎不像這樣的噴射機物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法立即存活下來 。 語言破壞了 , 試圖描述在其中一個噴射機中會是什麼樣子 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像是體驗超新星爆炸 , 但在指尖範圍和數百萬年的時間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射機發生在幾十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 有些化學物質可以精準地描述 , 模型 , 並且預測 , 最重要的是你的參考 , 在現實中發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個準確的工作模型 , 另一個方形的模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是超級正面的圖像 , 還包含了它 , 還包含了一種解釋性模型 , 包含了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 信念和這個結構相似 , 讓另一個結構隨著時間增加 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那個物理物體 , 不像彼此一樣 , 儘管它們是可能的 , 永遠無法體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是不同的化學圓柱 。 這個化學圓柱具有普遍性的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著 , 有史無前例的精準結構 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 是一個謙遜的中心 , 包含了整個物理現實的本質 。 至於 , 到目前為止 , 物理定律允許這個實現 , 甚至使它實現 , 是物理世界最重要的事之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	太陽系和我們的環境如何在我們其餘的宇宙中獲得這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬•霍金的標記是真的 , 但那是錯誤的強調 。 有一件事情是不對的 。 沒有任何特殊的物理 。 沒有特殊的干擾 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它只是我們在這裡所擁有的三樣東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是很重要的 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理 。 資訊處理是計算 , 電腦不需要知道如何製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體產生效應 , 來記錄我們發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放的知識、解釋 , 都是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	例如牛頓的重力定律大約300年前
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們以前所做的證據在地球上每一平方公尺 , 數十億年前 , 將會持續下去數十億年 。 所有其他的科學都一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	至於我們所知 , 證據發現所有科學中最基本的真相 , 只是為了我們的星球而已 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星際空間中 , 這三個基礎的開放式知識是他們最低的供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 它是空的 , 它很冷 , 很暗 , 還是很暗 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	實際上 , 這只是另一個理論的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為 , 想像一個立方體存在於星際空間中 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 立方體非常空 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造自動控制的太空站 , 那裡有一群科學家 , 致力於創造一個開放的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	超越現在的科技 , 甚至從星際空間收集氫氣 , 形成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個不可思議的宇宙中 , 如果有些東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼能阻止我們去做 , 除了知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識 , 而非資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動進行能源供應 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	同樣地 , 它對人類的感官很暗 。 但你只需要用望遠鏡 , 即便是現今的設計 , 外頭看 , 和我們從這裡看到的一樣的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你可以看見星星 , 和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠做到天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理、化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最難做的事可能是生物學領域的探險 , 因為要花上幾億年才能到達最近的生命行星 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴你們 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有像生物田野旅行那麼過 , 我想我們能在幾億年內完成 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以 , 事實上 , 星際空間包含了所有開放知識的開放空間 。 任何在宇宙中 , 任何地方 , 都可以變成我們一樣的謙卑 , 如果知道如何做到的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並不是獨一無二的宿主 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星際空間能夠創造出一個開放式的解釋 , 那幾乎是所有其他的環境 。 這就是地球 。 這就是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很龐大 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種宇宙知識基礎的觀點或許我認為應該讓我們覺得很特別 , 但也應該讓我們覺得脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 沒有必要的知識來生存宇宙的挑戰 , 我們就不會生存 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要幾光年之外的超新星才能離開 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁rees最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都錯了 , 最重要的是對大規模毀滅性武器恐怖主義的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的生存機會 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在研討會上談到這一點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為機率是討論這個問題的正確分類 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他 , 我們可以存活下來 , 我們也無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它取決於偶然 , 不論我們是否能創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是史無前例的 。 物種總是滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終結了 。 所有存在過的物種和文明中 , 絕大多數的物種都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想做例外的話 , 我們唯一的希望就是利用分辨物種的特徵和文明的特徵 , 我們的特徵 , 和物理定律的特徵 , 我們的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋 , 新知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我現在把它應用到目前的爭議 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 只為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是物理學家 。 在全球暖化的過程中 , 我只是一名階層人 。 而合理的一點是要認真看待先進的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太晚無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果我們現在最好的選項是預防二氧化碳排放 , 例如京都議定書 , 它的限制是經濟活動 , 它的巨大成本是數百億美元 , 或其它的成本 , 那已經被任何合理測量了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者的動作甚至沒有進步解決這個問題 , 僅僅靠一點點 , 才能將它打開 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能在任何人意識到危險之前就已經太晚了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代 , 可能已經太晚了 , 當最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將預防數十億人的新冰河時代 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一課對我來說很明顯 , 我不知道為什麼它不公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們永遠不會知道 。 當我們知道即興災難 , 以及如何花費比災難本身的成本低 , 然後我們就不會太多爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預防的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個問題來解決 , 不只是問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	事實是 , 一堆預防等同於一磅的療法 , 但只有我們知道該預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你在鼻子上被打了 , 那麼醫學的科學並不一致地教你如何避免打擊 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學學不再尋求治療和專注於預防 , 那麼它就不會達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	當時世界正在忙著計劃 , 來強迫氣體排放減少 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計劃來減少溫度 , 並且用計劃來生活在更高的溫度 , 而不是全部的成本 , 而是有效率且便宜的 。 有些計劃存在於空間中的鏡子 , 來反射陽光 , 並且鼓勵更多的生物 , 來吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此刻 , 這些研究都是費力研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力面對這個問題 , 一般來說 , 也不是問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們尚未察覺到的難題 , 不是不知不覺的好運 , 我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石頭表 , 放在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中之一 , 卡夫: 「 問題很容易解決 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一張車上: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家要如何破壞貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不好的規則中 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默揭露了一個大膽的想法: 「 查核城市 」 , 市區的行政區被國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治議題、政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅羅•羅門的極端點子:查特城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它對我們來說是一個非常有趣的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場上做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有任何電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到了像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	咱們來挑一個例子 , 綠色襯衫中的一個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	讓我們給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson能夠取得先進技術 , 像是手機 , 但沒有一個100歲的科技能在家裡發電燈光 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	用一個詞來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防這種雙贏解決方案 , 讓人們可以帶進新的科技 , 讓它們成為像尼爾森這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	在這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 說它必須在很低、很低的價格下賣電 , 事實上 , 價格非常低 , 每單位銷售的價格都很低 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它沒有資源 , 也沒有激勵力 , 去接觸其他的使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到可以有不同的規則 , 讓企業賺到小利潤 , 所以他們有獎勵來簽名更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這種規則是尼爾森購買了他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電力的規則 , 但他進入了企業和消費者的激烈抗議活動 , 他們想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	他被困住了規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在街燈下學習 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們能改變規則的方法 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有一些規則可以用來改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說 , 我們能做出實用的抽象觀點 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多選擇 , 在許多國家中 , 領導者也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間的相反是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導人的選擇 , 像是給總統提供電力的選擇 , 取代經濟的人們所想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇繼續消耗補助電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你給另一邊或另一邊 , 你會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更多選擇的方法 , 那就能給我們一套改變規則 , 來讓我們脫離陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能取得網際網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想要看到規則的破壞效應 , 規則能讓人們在黑暗中保持在黑暗中 , 看一下地球的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲人 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 這裡的線上 , 就像黑洞和鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會很驚訝地發現北韓的規則會讓人們在黑暗中保持在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 要了解到北韓和南韓的規則在兩種法律和規範的層面上是很重要的 , 但也在更深層的理解、文化、價值觀和信念上 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開後 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致了非常多樣化的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	我們可以改變人類的改變 , 改變我們彼此互動的規則 , 更好 , 或更糟糕 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在讓我們看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 在外線這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 與鄰居相比 , 多明尼加共和國有相同數量的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	兩個國家都比較黑暗 , 相較於波多黎各 , 有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加州共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則不好 , 因為政府太強、太壓迫 , 就像北韓 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造出有良好的規則的環境 , 我們就不能直接撕裂 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法來建構 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展示了規則的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的初期 , 中國是世界上高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅的技術 , 像是鋼、印刷、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則來鼓勵這些點子的傳播 , 一個獲利的動機 , 可以鼓勵散播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了減緩創新的規則 , 讓中國脫離世界其他地方 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界其他國家的創新 , 發展新科技 , 同時也發展新的規則 , 中國的規則被切斷了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入保持穩定 , 當它在世界其他地方放大 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一個圖表比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	美國平均收入佔美國平均收入的比例 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到它大約佔百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末 , 有些改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的經濟成長迅速地趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回到地圖上 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 導致中國的規則改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地點 , 這裡的邊緣是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是一小部分中國 , 在20世紀大部分的中國 , 在完全不同的規則下運作 , 和當時的勞動市場經濟規則 , 被英國政府管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 像是縫製襯衫、玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 導致非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典範 , 像是英國xiaoping能複製的領導者 , 當他們決定把所有的大陸都移到市場模型中 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但 , 英國的xiaoping直覺地了解到 , 給予他人選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫在中國的每個人立即轉變到市場模式上 , 他們建立了一些特殊的區塊 , 在某種意義上 , 英國所做的是:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 和想要選的人一起合作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創造了四個特殊的經濟區 , 在那裡中國人可以來工作 , 城市很迅速地成長 ; 外國企業可以進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的區塊有一個叫做 「 希曼 」 的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一間台台灣公司 , 製作了iphone , 在座的各位 , 他們用中國人搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特區之後 , 有14個海岸的白蟻 , 以相同的方式開放 , 最終在這些地方證明了人們可以選擇的成功 , 由於他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	顯示成功導致了整個經濟體的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了幾個點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保留人民的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的規模運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村落的規則 , 你就能做到 , 但一個村落太小了 , 要是你有數百萬人在良好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看事情是怎麼發生的 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會創造新的地方 , 讓人們可以採取行動的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們大到足以取得我們能擁有的所有利益 , 只要我們在好的規則下工作 , 就能有足夠的利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以提議是我們構想一個叫做 「 查爾特城市 」 的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 來吸引我們所需要的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引那些會建造電力系統的投資者、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 誰會僱用先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭、會來居民 , 永遠住在那裏 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子受教育 , 讓他們第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那張圖表 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一次又一次地進行 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它成功 , 我們需要良好的規則 , 我們已經討論過 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都是在圖表裡捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	若我們能在未居住的土地上建造城市 , 那就建成了這個模型 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新特區 , 但沒有人被迫住在那裡 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	我們最需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要領導者的選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作 , 讓國家團結在一起 , 實際上 , 讓中國和英國團結起來 , 建立一個小小的市場模型 , 然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意的透過香港的行動 , 來減少世界的貧窮 , 遠比我們在上個世紀所遭受的所有援助計畫 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們能讓這種合作夥伴再次複製 , 我們就能讓世界各地的規模受益 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的刪除 , 一個國家的控制權 , 從一個國家到另一個國家 , 取代某些政府的責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說 , 你們當中有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這會帶來殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	這不是 。 但要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 會出現的情緒 , 可能會讓我們鬆開心胸 , 試圖探索新點子 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	關於殖民主義的壞事 , 以及我們一些援助計畫中的壞事 , 就是它涉及了衝突和意識的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是為領導者 , 以及未來會活在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是對強迫和自閉症的抗藥性 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何在實務上演奏 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們帶領一個特定的領導者雷爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	肯定是為了卡斯楚 , 他有機會為古巴做些什麼 , 但他沒有在古巴島的香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確在南方有一點點光 , 那裡有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	這裡有一塊區域 , 位於保塔納莫灣 , 在那裡 , 一項協定給美國負責一塊土地 , 這大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	克斯楚去了加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , 伊恩克有個可怕的問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 接管呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的政府區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新的城市在那裡建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們在附近有香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會拿回來 , 但這將會是將現代經濟和現代世界連結起來 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還會被試過哪裡呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到一個特殊區域的概念 , 讓人們可以選擇成為規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	這是一個改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人們不需要合作 , 讓人們採取行動 , 而相反的 , 合作是有力的 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以為長期投資者做出更可信的承諾 , 像是建造港口、建造道路 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們可以做出更可信的承諾 , 如果他們和一個夥伴合作 , 就能得到更棒的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至有些安排有點像是escrow帳戶 , 讓土地進入escrow帳戶 , 和合作國會負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多土地可以建造新的城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸飛行的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	這裡有巨大的土地 , 像這樣的土地 , 那裡有數億人可以生存 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這個概念普遍化 , 想一想 , 不只是一兩個特殊的白蟻 , 還有數十個城市 , 能協助創造出數億個成千上萬的城市 , 也許數十億的居民會搬到來到來的城市 , 那裡有足夠的土地給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	世界各地 , 如果我們看夜間的燈光 , 有件事誤導了 , 視覺上來說 , 世上大部分的人都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我向各位說明為什麼會錯 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以所有土地的代表為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	將它轉變成地球上所有可耕地的方形 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已有三十億人口居住的城市 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到矩形的底部 , 你可以看到現有的三十億個都市居民佔地球上只有百分之三的可耕土地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要為其他數十億人建造城市 , 他們就會像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從可耕地的百分之三變成百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅減少地球上的人類足跡 , 藉由建造更多的城市 , 來建造更多的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則所管理 , 他們可以成為人們安全的城市 , 從疾病和不良衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會去找工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	它們可以得到基本的電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座慈善城市 , 我們要怎麼做才能建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它可以幫助手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的事就是寫一些細節 , 可以進入這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們跑城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者走出野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設它不僅僅是加拿大 , 還能處理種族監獄的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西也參與了西班牙也許古巴想要成為四個關節的夥伴之一
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫出治療方法 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	這樣做沒有前例 , 但那很容易就成功了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助呢 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是他們在一開始時所擁有的土地有很大的價值 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的收益來支付如警察、法庭 , 但學校和醫療保健體系 , 讓這個更吸引人的地方 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 意外 , 讓土地變得更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 人們幫助建造這個區域的激勵機制 , 建立基礎規則 , 走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	這裡還有很多其他的細節
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓在第一份工作中工作的人負擔得起低成本且負擔得起的建築物 , 像是iphone , 而是讓這些建築能有效率 , 並確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會落下地震或颶風 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術性的細節已經成功了 , 但那些已經開始追求這些東西的我們已經知道沒有道路 , 沒有任何障礙 , 除了想像的失敗之外 , 這讓我們無法實現真正的全球性的雙贏解決方 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來做結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能這麼順利 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像缺乏物品 , 分享的意義就越少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們就會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:我們和彼此互動的規則 ; 規則如 , 來支持研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	咱們來建立一個系統 , 讓土地擁有權限 , 在政府辦公室登記 , 讓人們可以當冷漠 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 尤其是創新規則 , 創造出改變規則的規則 , 所以我們不會被困住 , 那麼我們就能繼續進步 , 讓世界變得更好 , 讓像尼爾森和他的朋友不用再在街燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克萊格•凡特從他的史詩圓頂探險中休息 , 來談談他的團隊中數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 發現海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	克雷格•凡特在dna和海上 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對於老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我知道樂觀主義者是極度過時的悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴你們的是 , 我們將如何從閱讀基因編碼轉換到開始寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	直到十年前 , 我們才剛發表了第一序列的免費生物體 , 那種流感病毒感染 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫從13年到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加入了:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 數種昆蟲 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前 , 這種想法的基因組學 , 是在今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組序列 , 數百個 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金會得到一個補助 , 來到今年130個基因組 , 作為環保生物體的一邊專案 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但如我們所見 , 我們幾乎無法在這個星球上找到的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部份人都不知道 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球生物量的一半 , 而所有的動物只佔所有生物量的1/3 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人常常不會做的事 , 但如果你把它送到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的細菌 , 還有一千萬病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到5000種微生物在兩年前被特徵了所以我們決定要做點什麼
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了索托二次探險 , 在那裡 , 我們和偉大的海洋探險一樣 , 試圖在每200英里的海洋中進行樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在bermuda做實驗 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 橫跨太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常困難的一件事 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 協助讓年輕人興奮地進入科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只要將海水過濾 , 收集不同的大小生物 , 然後將它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時就能定序一億個基因密碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這樣做 , 我們發現了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 人們認為我們眼睛裡的視覺色素只有一個或兩個生物存在於環境中 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎全世界的所有物種都有相同的光接接收器 , 用陽光當它們的能量和溝通 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新的基因 , 大約五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經從sloan基金會中延伸到空氣 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量了我們所有人每天都在呼吸的病毒和細菌 , 尤其是在飛機或關閉的聽覺 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的顯微鏡過濾 ; 我們收集到來自紐約市的10億微生物 , 僅僅一天的濾水 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於當代的序列中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在資料集的這一邊 , 我們在加拉帕戈斯的一邊 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每兩百英哩的樣本中 , 我們看到海洋中的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合邏輯的 , 以不同溫度的層級來看 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 基於溫度紅色表示溫度 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫度和溫度樣本之間有著巨大的差異 , 以豐富的物種來說 ,
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們驚訝的事是這些光接收器偵測出不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些非常大的不同 , 從區域到區域 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外地 , 在深海裡 , 大部分是藍色的 , 光源接收器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有大量的染色體時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們會更加不同 , 可能會朝紅外線和紫外線走向極端 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了試著評估我們的基因再生是什麼 , 我們組裝了所有的資料 , 包括我們目前的考察 , 它代表了地球上所有基因資料的一半 , 總共有29百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些資料放進基因家庭 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但我們在環境中的每一種新樣本 , 都會在線性時期加入這些新家庭 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們正處於最早期的階段 , 發現這個星球的基本基因、元素和生命 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的演化樹 , 我們就站在右上角和動物的角落 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	其中大約有兩千九百萬個基因 , 我們的基因組中只有大約2萬4千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物聚集在一起 , 我們可能有不到三萬個 , 可能是十幾萬個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在一般的看法中 , 可能回到理查•達金斯的點子 , 和基因組成成的不同構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 已經改變了過去十年間dna定序的速度 , 越來越快 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們第一次想到合成基因組 , 是在1995年 , 我們將第二基因組序列列列 , 從菌絲體的生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我心臟的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	海豚有18000個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們簡單地問這個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 是否有一組較小的基因 , 可以組成一個最小的運作系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始進行轉型突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉移只是基因編碼中的一小塊dna隨機被隨機插入 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們在基因的中間插入 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們做了一張地圖 , 可以取代轉換的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 無生命基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 且你只能依據環境中的特徵來定義一個必要或正常的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智能方法來處理13種相關有機體的基因組 , 我們試著將這些基因組做比較 , 看看它們的共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們把這些重疊的圓圈 , 發現只有173個基因對所有13個有機體只有173個共同點 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一顆細胞寄生蟲 , 它會擴展到更多的核心基因 , 大約在310年左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴張或收縮基因組 , 取決於你這裡的觀點 , 大約300到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些點子的唯一方法就是建造一個人工染色體 , 裡面有這些基因 , 我們必須在以階層為基礎的時尚做這些 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片片片中合成的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hmsmith和clydehutchison , 我的同事開發了一種令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們能夠合成500000個鹼基對的病毒 , 僅僅在兩週內 , 以它的序列和它的生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是非常令人振奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注射到細菌中 , dna開始啟動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是最早的合成病毒 , 一年前就被製造出來的小兒麻痺病毒 , 但只有一個十公分的活性 , 花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個案例是軟體現在正在建造它自己的硬體 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上開始擔心生物戰事 , 我在參議院委員會之前就有了近期的證據 , 以及美國政府設立的一項特殊委員會 , 來審視這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要保持現實是很重要的 , 和人們的想像力有所不同 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何當今被列為序列的病毒 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會對伊波拉或天花感到驚訝 , 但這個生物體的dna並沒有感染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造天花基因組 , dna本身不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關心保安部門是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 試圖創造生物戰士 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真正不穩定 , 對於未來的設計者 , 應該有很少的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內是有可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能在十年之內 , 那些我們擁有的真核細胞是有可能的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以現在我們正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變種類和基因 , 轉換成人造染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 你要如何把所有其他人都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一套全新的重新組合系統 , 將它們組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一種有機體中衍生出來的 , 腎上腺素 , 可以承受三百萬種放射線 , 而不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它在輻射爆發後重新組合它的基因組 , 大約12到24小時後 , 染色體分開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個有機體在地球上無所不在 , 也許現在就存在於外太空 , 由於我們的旅程 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一台玻璃洗衣機 , 大約有50萬種輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 而底部的微生物變得更快樂和更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一張真實的照片 , 上面顯示了一百七十萬個輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體的分裂 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種 , 如果沒有數萬種 , 在這個星球上不同的物種 , 可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還對環境和社會議題有希望 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 我們序列的第三種生物甲烷佔據了生命的沸騰水溫 ; 它的能量來源是氫和碳 , 來自環境的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數以千計的不同生物 , 可以從二氧化碳中獲取回收 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 我們不用石油來製造合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳並從大氣中捕捉它 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物存在於二氧化碳中 , 以減少水分分分解 , 產生氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有數條路徑可以被工程代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一個很大的程式 , 用挪威的雕像來捕捉和將甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短短的一段時間內 , 我認為會有一種新的領域叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有這些新的合成能力 , 這些巨大的基因庫重新組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來製造一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 隨著所有生物學 , 你通過篩檢得到選擇 , 不論你是否在篩檢氫產品 , 或化學製品 , 或僅僅可見 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的作用 , 就會很接近 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試圖修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是來自氧氣的調節 , 我們有氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合細胞 , 分解複雜糖的酵素 , 變成簡單的糖 , 在同一個細胞中製造乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	用微生物 , 製藥生產已經在主要的實驗室裡 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學物質比我們最好的化學家所能產生的複雜性還要多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境的排放 , 或許可以取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年推行了我們的實驗 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 來評估我們是否該嘗試並製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖都用它們的文字作為法律書籍 , 他們找不到任何東西 , 所以它是可以的 。 唯一的關注是生物戰事方面的尊重 , 但給了我們這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會剛剛資助了多個機構的研究 , 來找出社會的風險和利益 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 例如我自己應該在這個領域中使用的規則 , 而我們正試著設定好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 我們可以設計產品來製造乾淨能源 , 也許革命化出開發中國家能做的事 , 透過各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•辛巴多說快樂和成功是根深蒂固的:我們傾向於過去、現在和未來的方式 。 他建議我們追求追求的第一步 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、生意、快樂、心智、心理學、科學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普•辛巴多開了一段健康的時間 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的一些想法 , 很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始時鐘 。 三十秒 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 。 安定下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	重點是時間 , 結束順序 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10 , 9 , 8 , 7 , 6 , 5 , 4 , 3...
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	philipzimbardo:咱們來談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來亞當 , 不要太願望了 。 請稍微說一下 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 , 不要棄eve 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好的 , 一口 , 什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑 。 重點在於 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 後來 , 衝動 , 反思 , 現在和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	保證美德會落入當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的女孩 , 她們承諾性抽象和處女 , 直到婚前 , 感謝布希大部分人 , 60% , 得到性誘惑 , 在一年內 , 為性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都不用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	承諾太多了 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們誘惑四歲的孩子 , 給他們一份治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就能有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等等 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	接下來發生的是三分之二的孩童給誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	當然 , 他們不能等 。 其他人當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 14年後回來 , 試圖發現那些孩子的差異 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	孩子們有很大的差異 , 抗拒和孩子 , 以許多方面來說 , 他們都有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒250分的孩子在土地上比較高 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像是一組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有那麼麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且決心的 。 今天對我來說 , 關鍵是 , 他們是未來的對象 , 而不是現在的對象 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將人類經驗的流向分成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動進行 , 無意識地進行 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化、國家、個人之間、社會階級之間、教育程度之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏見 , 因為你會學會克服其中的一些 , 且會破壞他人 。
what determines any decision you make ?	什麼決定你做出的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你決定要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人而言 , 只有在立即的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你在做什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	那些人 , 當他們在那個形式中做出決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 簡報 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的狀況 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說: 「 我過去經歷過什麼樣的情況 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們打算稱這些人為 「 牧師 」 , 因為他們專注於什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點在於預期後的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 將來 」 。 他們的焦點是 「 未來 」 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想爭論時間觀點的悖論 , 是影響你所做出的每個決策 , 你完全不知道的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有一個偏見 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以呈現出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被貼上過去 , 兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在貼紙上或貼紙上 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你也可以是指甲主義者 , 把焦點放在生命的喜悅 , 或現代主義者 , 無所謂 , 你的人生被控制 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:生命始於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展靈活性靈活性來改變時間觀點 , 取決於情況的需求 , 那就是你必須學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時間檔案 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	積極度積極 。 將來 , 高度積極 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	而現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於過去的負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的臨時混合是你從過去的主流中得到的 , 讓你的家人、身份、自我連結 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的 , 是翅膀 , 轉向新的目的 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的 「 享樂主義 」 中得到的能量 , 來探索你自己、地方、人們、感官 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間的觀點都比正面更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	成功的未來犧牲了什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲了家人的時間 , 他們犧牲了友誼 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲好玩的時光 , 犧牲個人的侮辱 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 。 他們犧牲了睡眠 。 所以它影響了他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活在工作、成就和掌控之中 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我確信ted的一些人會產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	它對我產生共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯hetto的一個貧窮孩子長大 , 一個西里亞的家庭 , 每個人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我在這裡 , 身為一個未來人 , 走過頂端的人 , 做了這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的人 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃棉花糖 , 因為如果你等待你 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了現在的指南主義 , 我把焦點放在過去的正面上 , 所以 , 在76歲的時候 , 我比以往更有活力 , 而且我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正在應用在許多世界問題上:改變輟學率 , 改變學童的輟學率 , 加強青少年的健康 , 用時間比喻來治療創投者 , 來促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體的復甦率 , 改變了自殺恐怖分子的死亡率 , 改變了家庭的死亡率 , 改變了家庭的衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我要說的是:許多生命的謎題都能被理解 , 和其他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很顯而易見 , 但我認為 , 後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今的頭條有多少人在一百年內會很重要 ? 一百年 ? 一百年 ? 柯蒂•克隆的《漫長新聞》收集故事 , 不只有今天 , 數十年 , 甚至會在ted2010年 , 他的頭條有潛力可以塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是:
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞中被淹沒 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是光是每年就有350萬個新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來說 , 這些故事會很重要嗎 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	它是一個由tedsters所創立的專案 , 包括kevinkelly和stewart品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們所期待的是新聞故事 , 可能在50、100、1000年後仍然重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過那過濾過來看新聞 , 就會因此跌倒了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	為了從a.p.這個上層的故事 , 去年 , 這會影響到十年嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會發生什麼事嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 這真的很酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 過去一年的頂尖故事是經濟 , 我打賭 , 不久後 , 這種特殊的衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	咱們來談談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血流 , 來修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 就已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂和真實蜂箱的腫瘤 ; 它們把基因送到大腦 ; 他們建造的機器人可以爬過人體 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵養九十億人口 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在有了60億人的營養問題 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國沒有基因改造的作物 , 英國會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茨已經打賭了十億人在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會變得非常不一樣 , 如果中國定下了議程 , 他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超越了美國最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超越了德國最大的出口國 , 他們開始在孩子們做dna測試 , 選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各式各樣的方法來推動我們所知的限制 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:阿根廷有一個螞蟻群 , 現在散播到每個大陸 , 但南極洲都有自主的機器人科學家 , 很快就會發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命可能就不再需要我們了 ; 一萬兩萬年之後 , 微生物醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 看似沒有我們 , 生命會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但 , 過去一年 , 我挑選了上頭的長篇新聞 , 就是這個:在月球上找到水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群在那邊放得更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不會這麼做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某個人可能會寫一份大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家carolynporco展現了卡西尼航海的影像 , 聚焦在它最大的衛星上 , 土衛六上 , 和冰川上 , 似乎是射擊冰的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa、設計、探索、科學、科學、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡林•普科把我們帶到土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的18分鐘 , 我要帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程是你和我過去多年的旅程 , 從50年前開始 , 人類第一次踏出地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	而在那50年裡 , 我們不僅僅在月球上設立了腳 , 還在所有行星上 , 我們已經把機器人太空船送到所有八個行星上 , 我們已經登陸了彗星 , 此時此時此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 可以將它稱為星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是更大的人類旅程之一:一趟旅程 , 去了解宇宙的地方 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球、地球、我們 , 都生活在其中 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中 , 我們可能要去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 有土星 。 在1980年代早期 , 我們去過土星 , 但我們對土星的調查越來越深 , 自從卡西尼太空船以來 , 旅行跨越了七年 , 讓土星繞著土星繞行 , 在2004年的土星繞行 , 變成了人類史上最遙遠的太空 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個豐富的星球系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞見 , 顯然的福利超越了這個系統的調查 , 已經超越了宇宙的範圍 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究環圈 , 我們就要學習很多關於星球和氣體的距離 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是andromedanebula的美麗照片 , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大的螺旋銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	然後 , 這裡有一個美麗的旋律銀河系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程是真正的一部分 , 也是人類的旅程 , 來了解我們周遭的所有事物之間的連結 , 以及人類如何符合這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我感到痛苦 , 我不能告訴你們我們在卡西尼學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看過去兩年半以來我們拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
