so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我將集中在兩個最令人振奮的故事中 , 出現在這個主要的探險探險旅程中 , 我們在土星周圍進行了兩年半 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著非常大且多樣化的衛星 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的尺寸和幾公里的大小一樣 , 橫跨到美國 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝土星的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星和一些衛星一起 , 這裡是土星 , 這裡是土星 , 這裡是土星 , 這裡是土星邊緣 , 顯示土星是多麼的薄 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆月中有兩個是站立的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛二 。 土衛六是土衛六最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼到達那裡 , 是我們太陽系中最大的未知範圍 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是一種長久以來觀察行星的人的身體 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有一個很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像是地球上的環境 , 或者 , 至少在過去的太陽系中 , 比任何其他的身體還多 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層大多是分子氮 , 就像你在這房間裡呼吸一樣 , 除了大氣中 , 它的大氣層被簡單的有機物質困惑 , 比如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在土衛六大氣層中被破壞 , 它們的產品會結合在一起 , 製造出黑粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	牠是無所不在的 。 牠完全是全球性的 , 包裹著土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你不能用我們的眼睛在光譜中看到的 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些黑色的粒子 , 它被保證在我們和卡西尼一起到那裡之前 , 數十億年來 , 溫和地漂移到表面 , 將表面覆蓋在厚的有機液體中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	如同泰坦一樣 , 泰坦和油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以在土衛六的表面溫度 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是向土衛六的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣層中是可以凝聚的 , 所以意識到這種情況 , 帶到整個世界 , 奇怪的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在雲層之上 , 你有上百公里的哈西 , 可以防止任何陽光到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但即使如此寒冷 , 你也可能在鐵達尼的表面下降 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上下雨的作用:它會照顧衛星 , 它會形成河流和貓 ; 它能在大盆地上創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石上池塘 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把山峰和山丘沖掉 , 沖到低地 , 停下來 , 想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 泰坦的高點跟地球的深處一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很噁心 , 很可能會下雨 , 你可能站在密西根湖的門上 , 用油漆薄的門上 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在土衛六和土衛六的表面之前 , 我可以告訴你們我們在土衛六的發現 , 雖然在土衛六的情況下 , 其實並不一樣 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 它就像是卡西尼人 , 它就像是果蠅verne冒險一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說的 , 它有一個厚厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是泰坦的照片 , 太陽的背景 , 環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是一個非常巨大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號有樂器可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的攝影機是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 就跟我們一樣 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在是太神秘了:我們無法搞清楚我們在泰坦所看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你更仔細地看這個區域 , 你就會開始看到我們不知道的東西 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 事實上 , 一個坑洞 , 但在土衛六表面上有很少的坑洞 , 意思是 , 它是非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來很特徵 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來像是被拆開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在地球上看到任何線條 , 就意味著有破碎 , 像是斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一件事件 , 許多人被視為是鐵達尼的調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那就是 「 huygens探測器 」 的部署 , 歐布萊特•哈根探測器在整個太陽系運行了七年 。 我們把它部署到泰坦大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時才下降 , 它降了地表 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這個事件有多麼重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它是人類史上第一次登陸太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	很顯著 , 在我心中 , 這事件應該被讚揚在美國和歐洲和歐洲的每個城市都市的膠帶遊行 。 很遺憾的是 , 這並不是事實 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	另一個原因是 , 這是國際的使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國慶祝 , 而慶祝的演講則是用英語口音、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個移動的示範 「 聯合國 」 應該代表的是:一個真正的國家團結 , 加入了對好的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 它是一個巨大的探索一個星球 , 來了解一個人類歷史的星球系統 , 而現在人類已經觸及了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我是說 , 我正在談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是非常情緒化的事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器在降落大氣層的測量值 , 它也拍攝了全景的照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 第一次從探測表面看泰坦的表面是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是震驚了 , 因為我們希望其他照片從軌道上拍下來 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是個不可知的模式 , 一個地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種垂直的飲料模式 , 只能由液體流來形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追隨這些頻道 , 你可以看到它們是如何融合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們把這個頻道轉換成這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片拍攝了8公里 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大概是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要穿過美國的飛機旅行 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這是你在鐵達尼亞航空的窗戶上 , 飛越鐵達尼號的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器出現在表面上 , 我要給你們看 , 女士們先生們 , 第一個從外太陽系的表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰石石 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它降落在一個平面、黑暗的區域 , 而它沒有被視力淹沒 。 所以它不是我們登陸的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上 , 探測器的成分相當於泥土平 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是個不合理的土地 , 上面有液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	這可能是我們透過這些頻道將鐵達尼號的高地沖掉 , 經過數十億年的水平 , 來填滿低水平 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是huygens探測器登陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 我們的影像中仍然沒有徵兆 , 或甚至在液體的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	牠們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 牠們變得更令人驚訝 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們電影的泰坦方形區域 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些是一百公尺高的沙丘 , 分開了幾公里 , 幾英里 , 幾英里 , 幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百、1000或1千英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是泰坦沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會有沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次地 , 它有點困惑 , 沒有液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到北極地區的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在南極的鐵達尼地區 , 有一個湖 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約和安大略湖一樣大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 只有一週半前 , 我們飛越了鐵達尼亞北極 , 再一次地發現 , 我們發現了一具特色的特色 , 就跟加賽海一樣大 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以看似液體 , 原因是我們不了解的 , 或者至少這季 , 顯然是鐵達尼號的兩極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是個很了不起、神秘的地方 。 它是外星人 , 但卻是很奇怪的地質形狀 , 讓像地球的地質多樣性和極大的地質多樣性 , 一個令人著迷的世界 , 只有在太陽系的複雜度和豐富度本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 , 土衛二是小型月球 , 大約是土衛六的尺寸 。 你可以在這裡看到 , 這裡是英格蘭的大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 非常明亮 , 它的表面很明顯被破碎 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一個非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二的媽媽在南極發現了發現 , 我們在南極 , 發現了這種碎形系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋 。 這些碎片被有機物質覆蓋 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整個區域 , 南極區域有高溫 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就像是發現在地球上的南極比熱帶還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍攝額外的圖片 , 我們發現 , 來自這些碎形的噴射 , 冰粒會延伸到太空中數百英哩 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們將這張影像編碼 , 將微弱的光源帶出去 , 我們看到這些噴射線餵飽了一量 , 事實上 , 在其他影像中 , 數千英哩進入了土衛六的太空 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊發現了像這樣的圖像 , 像這張圖片 , 想起了卡西尼號的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射可能是從土衛六表面底部的液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們可能有液態水、有機物質和多餘的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 現代化日星球探索的聖杯可能是適合生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們 , 我們太陽系其他地方的生命發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意義 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明基因有一次發生 , 而不是一次發生 , 而是兩次獨立 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就意味著 , 在整個宇宙中 , 它發生了很驚人的次數 , 且它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍然是我們所知唯一的行星 , 仍然是生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 我們所知唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們之中有任何人在1960年代被警告 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果你不是 , 你還記得在1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍攝的這張很有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次地球是從太空而來的 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球的保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	首先 , 我們在卡西尼號拍攝了一張相片 , 前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全部蝕刻 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張不可思議的圖片中 , 你可以看到太陽的主環 , 你可以看到太陽的重建影像 , 實際上 , 由土衛六的延伸而產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 彷彿那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以發現 , 在這個美麗的圖像中 , 看見我們自己的星球 , 陷入土星的環節 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些關於從afar看自己的東西 , 並且捕捉到我們小小的藍色星球 , 在其它世界的天空中 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	這也是我們從中得到的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這趟旅程中得到最好的獎賞 , 開始了半個世紀 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	至於2005年 , 只有15%的人被繪製了 。 這慢慢地造成災難的援助 , 隱藏了未知的土地和未知的道路 。 在短短的演說中 , google的katradademadademostr , 一群全球的人們使用地圖來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	遲緩卡達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建造經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , cyclonenagis破壞了我的anmar 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人受到嚴重的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要壓迫人民 , 供應整個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有協助協助到達西哥的受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖 , 很難相信在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地理位置 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國執行總部陷入一個問題 , 世界上絕大多數的民眾臉:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助要來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40位志工使用新的軟體來繪製120萬公里的道路、3000間醫院、物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? google繪圖機 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖製造者是一項賦予我們每個人在地圖上所知的科技 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製每樣東西 , 從道路到河流、學校、當地企業 , 到視頻商店到角落的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名赫南多德•索托承認 , 大部分開發中國家的經濟訴訟的關鍵是要把大量未被統治的土地上標籤 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 僅僅在印度 , 數兆美元的房地產仍然不足 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 170個國家的數以千計的使用者就繪製了數百萬個資料 , 並且創造出一個史無前例的細節 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	由熱情使用者的力量實現 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在讓我們來看看一些用戶製作的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 如我們所說的 , 在170個國家 , 人們正在繪製世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到非洲的橋樑 , 剛在塞內加爾畫了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家更近 , 查盧亞 , 一個在班加羅爾的n.道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學的結果 , 手勢認可 , 機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市 , 一個使用者 , 一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們未開發的地球70%的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 佛教村落的巴勒斯坦村落在十個月的非暴力抗爭中 , 阻止了他們在橄欖的烤箱上建造的障礙 。 你聽說了嗎 ? 不這麼認為 。 巴西製片師朱利亞•巴契亞問:為什麼我們只關注以色列的暴力 , 而非暴力的領袖 , 而非暴力的領導人 , 會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱莉亞•巴契亞:專注於非暴力 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的方式結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰是 , 我剛從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了數十位巴勒斯坦人使用非暴力來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和居民 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正試圖忘記一個龐大的國家非暴力運動 , 來結束職業 , 並在這個地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在這片地上和國外的認知之間的分歧 , 正是我們尚未成功的巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	今天我來這裡談談關注的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及在西岸的非暴力運動發展 , 加薩和其他地方 , 但我的案件研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大部份的成長並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是為了我們開始關注那些已經有的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明這個點 , 帶你到這個叫做布德魯斯的村落 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建造一個隔離障礙 , 而這個障礙會在村莊的頂端 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去百分之四十的土地 , 圍繞著土地 , 所以他們會自由地取得西岸 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過啟發當地的領導力 , 他們發起了和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的片段 , 讓你們知道在地面上看起來是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆會和以色列分離巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在佛羅斯這裡 , 我們發現牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:柵欄其實已經創造出了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十個以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列激進分子:軍隊沒有比非暴力反對更嚇人 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但他們沒有人能這麼做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	fatah黨員:我們必須擁抱傳統思維的思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想要把它散播給所有的巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫 , 哈馬斯和受歡迎的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持:在柵欄上 , 口號持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何武力 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活生的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	它就像夏洛伊賈 。 到處都是槍擊 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列激進分子:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊 , 有些人甚至還沒有更新 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭不會阻止[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	蛋白質:這是和平遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	沒有必要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	主持人:我們可以做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴cha:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我驚訝的是國際媒體並沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 佛陀成功的事實 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民在10個月的和平抗性後 , 說服以色列政府搬出他們的土地和綠線 , 也就是國際認可的界限 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦的領土 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	佛祖的抗藥性已經擴散到西岸的村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然沉默於這些故事中 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默的後果對非暴力的可能性有很深的後果 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抵抗和非暴力抵抗 , 共享一件非常重要的事 ; 兩者都是劇院尋求他們的成因 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力的演員是唯一不斷地在前版報導 , 吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題 , 這對非暴力的領導者來說是非常困難的 , 讓他們的社區成為公民不服從的一種可行的選擇 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對房間裡的父母毫無意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓孩子們更大聲地扔下去 , 最確切的方法就是讓他第一次注意到他丟下一套套套裝置 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	幻肢會成為童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子學到 , 他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以激勵或分散的行為 , 單單單是給孩子或戒斷注意力 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可能會受到影響 , 取決於國際社區選擇專注的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東衝突的核心 , 將和平帶給我們 , 將非暴力行為轉化為一種功能性的行為 , 讓非暴力領導者更加關注現今在地面上的非暴力領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我在西岸的村落、加薩和東耶路撒冷的過程中 , 我看到了即使只有一部紀錄片都能影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉吉的村落 , 很靠近耶路撒冷 , 社區正面臨著非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去許多土地 , 沒有取得權利 , 不論是西岸還是耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力手段了大約兩年 , 但從沒有人注意到他們 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一支螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉辦了最熱門且最明確的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民看到布德魯斯紀錄片裡的布德魯斯的故事 , 覺得確實有人追蹤他們在做的事 , 人們關心的 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一種新的和平運動叫做索里達特 , 意思是希伯來語的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者被用作他們主要的招募工具 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導以色列從未活躍過的人 , 看電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華拉吉和索里運動的例子顯示即使是一部小型的預算獨立電影也能扮演非暴力行為的角色
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週非暴力的示威 , 像是bil'in、nilin , 華拉 , 在耶路撒冷的社區中 , 例如sikhjarrah和silwan , 非暴力的領導者會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不關心這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像從未發生 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是我第一次看到如果我們這麼做 , 它們會乘上 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們乘上 , 他們的影響力會在以色列的巴勒比亞衝突中生長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力就是能夠解開這個情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領袖已經證明非暴力在布德魯斯這樣的地方工作 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給予他們注意力 , 讓他們在各地都能證明它是有效的 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•松克有一個簡單又強而有力的靈感模式 , 始於黃金圓和問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括apple , 馬丁•路德•金 , 以及萊特兄弟 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	布爾西、企業家、企業家、領導力、銷售、成功、成功、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•松克:偉大的領導人有多麼激勵人心 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋 , 當事情不如我們假設時 , 事情會不會發生 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者 , 更好的是 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能夠做到似乎所有假設時 , 會如何 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	一年後 , 年復一年 , 比起所有的競爭都要有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	但 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才華、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼它們似乎有不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德•路德國領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一受苦於美國前任權利的人 , 他肯定不是那天唯一的偉大統治者 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為何萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控、發電飛行的力量 , 尤其是其他團隊更有資格、更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒能動手飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我發現了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這發現深深地改變了我的看法 , 改變了我對世界運作的看法 , 甚至徹底改變了我操作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有的偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 無論是蘋果或馬丁•路德•金或他們都認為的萊特兄弟 , 採取相同的溝通方式 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是將它編碼 , 它可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼辦 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠鼓舞別人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上每一個人 , 每一個組織都知道他們做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是怎麼做到的 , 不論你稱之為你的分化價值觀提議 , 或你的特殊程序 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做他們做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	根據 「 為什麼 」 我不指的是 「 做利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	結果是 , 結果總是如此 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂 「 為什麼 」 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼早上你要離開床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要關心 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們認為 , 我們採取行動的方式 , 我們的溝通方式來自外部 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 , 我們從最明顯的東西 , 到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵人心的領導人和激勵人心的組織 , 不論他們的大小 , 不論他們的產業都在思考、行動 , 以及從內部溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果 , 因為它們很容易理解 , 每個人都會得到它 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果跟其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息可能會像這樣: 「 我們會製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們設計得很漂亮 , 很容易使用 , 也很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 「 梅 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是大部分的行銷方式 , 大部分的銷售量都是如此 , 我們大部分的人都在互相交流 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做的事 , 我們說我們是不同的 , 或我們比較好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票 , 等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體哩 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是這樣的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方法是讓我們的產品美麗設計 , 簡單地使用和使用 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣嗎 ? 你準備好從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你做的事 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你做的事 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都很舒服地買一台蘋果電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很舒服地買一個蘋果電腦的mp3玩家 , 或是蘋果手機 , 或是蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何區別它們的競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都同樣合格製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 格蘭特電視台出現了 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們有能力製造平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在製造平面螢幕監測器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	德爾和pdas公司發表了一篇很棒的產品 , 他們能做出完美的產品 , 沒有人買到 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像買一個mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從一家電腦公司買一個mp3玩家 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你做的事 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和任何需要你所擁有的所有人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和那些相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最好的部分是:我所說的不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	這一切都在生物學的網絡裡 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的十字路口 , 從頂端看 , 你看到的是人類的大腦被分解成三個主要的元件 , 和黃金圈完全相連 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的人類大腦 , 我們的新皮質 , 和 「 什麼 」 相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性和分析思考和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個區塊構成了我們的邊緣腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為、所有決策 , 且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、利潤、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部傳遞訊息 , 我們直接和控制行為的大腦對話 , 接著 , 我們允許人們將它合理化 , 用我們說的話來做 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候 , 你可以給別人所有事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節是什麼 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制決策的部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的方法是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或有時你說你正帶著你的心 , 或帶著你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭打破它 , 這些不是其他身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦裡 , 控制決策的腦部 , 而不是語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼要做你做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼要做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或是從你身上買東西 , 或更重要的是 , 要忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你的東西的人 ; 目標是賣給相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你僱用人們 , 只因為他們能做工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你僱用那些相信你所相信的人 , 他們會為你工作 , 用血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	除了萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀初 , 權力飛行的追求就像白天的點 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley所設定的成就
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 你的產品為什麼會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你同樣的三件事的認知:低估、錯誤的人、壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	一直都是一樣的三件事 , 咱們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley給了五萬美金 , 由戰爭部門來找出這台飛行器 。
money was no problem .	金錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛的一席工作 , 在史密森尼亞工作 , 非常有聯繫 ; 他知道白天的所有偉大思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的心智 , 可以找到 , 而市場的狀況很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處追蹤 , 每個人都在為langley發聲 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們怎麼不會聽到samuelpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠在俄亥俄州的幾百英哩外 , 歐維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們付錢給他們的夢想 , 拿著他們的自行車店 , 不是在萊特兄弟的團隊裡的單人 , 他們有大學教育 , 甚至不是ville或wilbur ; 而紐約時報跟隨他們 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 歐維爾和威爾布爾被一個原因所驅動 , 由一個信念所驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能找出飛行器 , 就能改變世界的軌跡 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要富有 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求財富 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	再看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想 , 和他們合作 , 帶著血汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只為了付款而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每次萊特兄弟會出去 , 他們會需要五組零件 , 因為那是他們在供應商之前會碰到多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟拍了飛機 , 沒有人會在那裡體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了這件事 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	此外 , 拉格利被錯誤的動機給激勵了:萊特兄弟採取飛行 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 這真是太棒了 , 各位 , 我會改善你的科技 , 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是首先 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你做的事 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的人很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一個叫做創新的定律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5%是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們的初選者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你最早期的大多數人 , 最晚的階級 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買到手機的唯一理由 , 是因為你再也買不起手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在不同的時間點 , 在這個尺度上 , 但創新的定律告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾的成功或大眾接受這個想法 , 你就不能有它 , 直到你在15%到18%的市場滲透 , 然後系統的尖端 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新生意有什麼影響 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很樂意跟你說: 「 喔 , 這大約是10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	你可以超過百分之十的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約百分之十的 「 去做 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	這就像是那種感覺: 「 喔 , 他們才懂 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到在你和他們一起做生意之前得到的那些 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以這就是這個小小的鴻溝 , 如同jeffreymoore所說的 , 「 跨越混亂 」 , 因為 , 早期大部分的人都不會嘗試直到別人試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們很舒服地做出這些腸道決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們比較舒服地做出他們相信世界的直覺決策 , 而不只是產品是可用的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站在線上六個小時買一支iphone , 當他們第一次出門時 , 只要走進商店 , 買下一週的商店 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面螢幕上 , 第一次出櫃時 , 雖然這項技術是被訂閱的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便說一下 , 他們並沒有這麼做 , 因為科技很棒 , 他們為自己做得到 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想要成為第一名 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不購買你所做的事 ; 他們買你做的事 , 僅僅是證明你所相信的事 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們在頭六個小時內買iphone的原因 , 是因為他們相信這個世界 , 以及他們希望每個人看到他們:他們是第一人 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你做的事 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及一個有名的創新法則的成功 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們之前所說的 , 成功的食譜是金錢和對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八到九年前 , tivo就出現了 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常富裕 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是把垃圾時間華納的dvr綁在我的垃圾桶上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一個商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是三十或四十美元 , 然後爆發 , 並且從來沒有在十歲以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它的交易高於6 , 除非有幾個小煙霧 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo發射他們的產品告訴我們他們所擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一件可以暫停的電視、滑雪的商業性、改造現場的電視 , 不需要你問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	大部分的憤世嫉俗說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你人生的每一面 , 男孩 , 我們會為你做一個產品 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場的電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記憶你的觀點習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不購買你所做的事 ; 他們買你做的事 , 而你所做的僅僅是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個成功的例子來說明創新的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年的夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心 , 聽見金恩博士說話 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們完全沒有邀請 , 沒有網站來檢查日期 。
how do you do that ?	該怎麼做 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的統治者 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是唯一在美國受苦的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些點子很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們 , 要改變美國所需的 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處 , 告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的 , 取決於他的理由 , 他們自己創造了它 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造出了結構 , 讓更多人發出訊息 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	最後 , 有25萬人在右日出席 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們相信美國讓他們在八月中部旅行八個小時 , 站在華盛頓的太陽裡 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 不是黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信這世界上有兩種法則:那些被高權威所制定的法律 , 以及被人製造出來的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有由人類所制定的法律 , 都是由高權威制定的法律 , 我們會住在一個公義的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好發生了 , 民權運動是最好的一件事 , 協助他把他的成因帶到生命中 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一下 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 的演講 , 不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在請聽政治人物 , 用他們全心全意的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者和領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但領導者鼓舞我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們遵循那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導的人 , 而不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人有能力啟發他們周圍的人 , 或找到啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要如何記得你在哪裡停車 ? 你怎麼知道你是不是在正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家neil埋葬我們周遭的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索神經科學、科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大停車場 , 我們要如何記住車子的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	問題來了荷馬 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體 , 顯示黃色 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有受到傷害 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你無法記住事物 , 包括你車子的位置 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是以拉丁文命名的 「 海底 」 命名的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	如同大腦其他部位 , 是由神經元組成 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元彼此溝通 , 透過發送小脈衝或發射電流 , 彼此之間的連結 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬迴形成了兩塊細胞 , 密度非常緊密 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶如何運作 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元 , 或探索環境尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們會想像 , 我們在這個老鼠的海馬體中記錄一個神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一點點電力 , 就會有紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到的是這個神經元每當老鼠進入一個特定的環境
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會訊號到大腦其他部位 , 透過發送小小的電流 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	我們可以看到神經元的發育率是動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元記錄 , 我們會看到不同的神經元在它的環境中 , 比如這個方形盒中顯示的 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 他們在一起形成了大腦的地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	植入細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時會需要他們的大腦監控電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了個電玩遊戲 , 讓他們開車到一個小鎮 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體內的細胞會發射、活化、發射電脈衝 , 每當他們開車穿過城市的特定位置時 , 就會發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個位置細胞如何知道老鼠在其環境中的哪個位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界限尤其重要
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	頂部的上面有像螢火蟲在盒子牆壁之間發射 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴大盒子時 , 發出的位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的下面是要在南邊有一道牆 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放在盒子裡 , 細胞會在兩面牆上開火 , 只要動物在盒子裡四處探索 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	因此 , 這種預測 , 在你延伸建築物周圍的邊界和方向 , 尤其是海馬體的重要性 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入中 , 細胞會被發現哪些專案在海馬體中 , 會回應哪些界限 , 或特定的距離 , 以及從老鼠或老鼠到牠正在探索的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每當動物接近一面牆或東邊的邊界 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣或圓形牆 , 或甚至是圓形盒的邊緣 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會在南邊有界線 , 不論是桌子或牆的邊緣 , 或甚至是兩張桌子之間的差距 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以這就是我們認為將細胞的位置決定了牠正在探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物品的位置 , 像是這個目標旗 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或是你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 看看他們必須記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 如同我們和安慰細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果國旗在一個小方形的環境中 , 交叉的位置 , 那麼如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境更大 , 他們認為國旗在哪裡被延伸出去 , 讓它延伸出去 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就好像你記住旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存你位置的所有位置細胞的模式 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以最好配合你位置的位置 , 和那儲存的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在運動的位置 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們把一些外界的路徑 , 也許我們會停下來 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們就能整合這條路徑的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一種叫做網格細胞的細胞中取得這種通路 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞再次被發現 , 輸入海馬體 , 它們有點像是位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠在各處探索時 , 每個細胞都在各個不同的地點發射 , 在一個奇妙的三角形格子中 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從這裡記錄不同顏色的格子細胞 , 每一種顏色都有類似的電線 , 每一種細胞的電網 , 都跟其他細胞的電網有一點關係 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的這張圖表上有綠色的 , 上面有藍色的 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 結合起來 , 就好像老鼠可以把虛擬的電網放到它的環境中 , 有點像是你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線 , 但使用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	隨著它移動 , 電活動可以通過這些細胞傳到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的所在位置 , 讓它可以利用它自己的動作 , 來了解它在它的環境中 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因爲所有類似電網的電網都有相同的對稱軸 , 相同的電線 , 顯示在橘色中 , 也就是說 , 大腦中所有電網的神經活動應該要根據六個方向 , 或沿著六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	我們可以把人放在磁共振掃描儀裡 , 讓他們做一個小遊戲 , 就像我剛剛給你們看的 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人體內看到它 , 正如你在老鼠身上看到的一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車子在哪裡 , 那裡的距離和方向 , 來延伸建築和界限 , 讓他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	藉由激發細胞的激發來代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園走出來的路徑 , 會被電網電池所代表 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以製造位置細胞 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以返回位置 , 藉由移動的位置 , 找到最好符合他大腦中的位置細胞在儲存的模式 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到原點 , 虛擬暗示他的車是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許是被嚇到的 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找類似電網的旋轉模式 , 我們在一系列的位置中看到 , 當我們做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 總是活躍起來 , 比如記住你上次去婚禮 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 也許神經機制代表我們周遭的空間 , 也被用來產生視覺影像 , 讓我們能夠重現空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像它們時 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 以這些密度相互作用的密度來啟動彼此 , 然後重新啟動邊界細胞 , 來創造你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個視點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部導向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們會像你面對的那樣 , 像羅盤一樣大火 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要為你的視覺影像產生影像 , 所以你可以想像當你在婚禮時發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代在認知神經科學中的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 比如你如何記住或想像 , 甚至在數十億個神經元的行動中 , 產生我們的大腦 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 在機構、政府、私人部門和公眾之間合作的全球安全驅動力 。 這不僅僅是開放性粉絲的遙遠希望 , 也是納米•斯特里迪斯的最高指揮官 , 他們在近期的軍事歷史中分享了一些充滿活力的時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆士斯•斯瓦里迪:納托最高指揮官如何思考全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我今天要談的是開放資源安全 , 因為我們必須在21世紀得到更好的安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先讓我回顧20世紀 , 來了解一下安全的運作方式 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國南部的戰場 , 僅僅是比利時總部的北部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過三百天 , 七十萬人被殺害 , 所以每天大約有兩千人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它推向二十世紀的第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達林大學的戰役 , 三百天 , 有兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續嘗試建造圍牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的陷阱戰爭變成第二次世界大戰的模糊線 , 然後我們進入冷戰、鐵幕、柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我的今天論點是 , 我們不需要建造圍牆來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲最著名的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是位於愛伏尼亞河的橋樑 , 位於新穎的主題 , 它談到 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹半島 , 經過一段時間 , 已經有了巨大的牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去的十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫地 , 聚集在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我認為 , 公開資源安全是關聯國際、國際間、私人共識 , 並將它與策略溝通連結在一起 , 大多是在社交網路 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物以各種方式攻擊 , 而全球公有物沒有任何威脅會被建造牆所解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	它的側邊有音樂會電線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	piracy是世界各地非常活躍的威脅 。 這是印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	陰謀也非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它活躍於幾內亞灣 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	它是全球運輸系統中的10億美元 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500名軍人住宿 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉換到另一種海、網路海洋 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	那時 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 把他們網上超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟中的2兆美元 。
two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆人 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國國民生產毛額下的 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	這種網路海洋 , 我們無止境地知道這一塊極端的開放 , 也受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我擔心全球公有物的另一件事 , 就是被販賣的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片 , 來自阿富汗 , 歐洲到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心安地斯山脊北方的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的運動 , 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販運主要在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們這是一個非常高科技的美國海軍怪胎 , 用來阻止販運 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一種半數的毒品販 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美叢林裡建造出來的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用低科技的raft來抓住它 , 它帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個 , 複雜的溝通方式 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣方式 , 以人類、武器、上帝禁止大規模毀滅性的武器 , 是全球公有威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們一起在阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一片土地
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十到九十的人 , 來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也看到了恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是蓋達組織的地方 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的衝動 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以這恐怖主義的擔憂也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須處理的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	這裡是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具不會成功 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我敢說 , 我們不會只靠槍的桶子提供安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會直接從一桶槍的桶裡送出安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 更有競爭力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開源的安全是關於國際、國際間、私人的聯結 , 由於網路上的策略溝通 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子說明這如何以正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很怪 。 我以為我讀到這個人口、年輕男女 , 二十到三十歲時 , 大部分是阿富汗的象徵 。 」
you would be correct .	你是正確的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	百分之八十五的百分比無法讀取阿富汗的安全力量 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在這些男性和女性會學會閱讀時期的禁令教育 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裏 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們在教導他們閱讀文學課程 , 由南托和私人部門合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教導了超過二十萬名阿富汗安全部隊 , 以基礎的層面來閱讀和寫作 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你能在阿富汗閱讀和寫字時 , 你通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們帶著這筆筆很驕傲 , 把它放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這結合了國際間有50個國家參與了這個任務-國際關係--這些發展機構--這些是私人的公共機關 , 來承擔這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也在教導他們戰鬥技能 , 但我認為 , 開放資源安全意味著連結更長久的安全效應 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適感 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一個姐妹船叫做慈悲 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這張 , 舒適 , 在加勒比海和南美海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在典型的殘酷中 , 他們會做四十萬名病人的治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	這並不是軍隊 , 而是結合了人道主義組織:營運希望、計畫微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織會發送志工 。
interagency physicians come out .	實習醫生出來了 。
they're all part of this .	這些都是其中的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子來說 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲大 , 帶著他的母親走過兩天 , 來到舒適的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他滿身時 , 穿過他極度的肉眼時 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	把這個方法乘上四十萬名病人的治療 , 這種私人的民眾合作 , 用安全的力量 , 你開始看到創造安全的力量 , 以非常不同的方式來創造安全 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你可以看到棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能在這張照片中挑出兩位美國軍隊士兵嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這些年輕男孩的兩位年輕男生 。 這是一系列的棒球診所 , 我們在大聯盟棒球協作 , 國家部門設立了外交棒球比賽 , 軍事棒球選手 , 他們是真正的技能 , 但參與了這個使命 , 他們在拉丁美洲和加勒比亞、加勒比亞、宏都拉多 , 在美國和加勒比亞 , 建立了診所 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它向年輕男女榜樣展示關於健身和生活的典範 , 我會主張協助為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這合作關係的另一面是災難性的救援 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機在2004年後參加海嘯殺害了25萬人 。
